The Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma,
Chapter 1: Introduction
Thus have I heard. At one time, the Buddha was staying on Mount Vulture Peak in the city of Rajagriha, together with a great assembly of twelve thousand monks. All were Arhats, their defilements extinguished, their afflictions gone. They had attained their own benefit, cut all bonds of existence, and their minds had achieved liberation. Their names were: Ajñāta-Kauṇḍinya, Mahākāśyapa, Uruvilva-Kāśyapa, Gayā-Kāśyapa, Nadī-Kāśyapa, Śāriputra, Mahāmaudgalyāyana, Mahākātyāyana, Aniruddha, Kapphiṇa, Kauṇḍinya, Revata, Pūrṇa-Maitrāyaṇīputra, Subhūti, Ananda, Rāhula, and other great Arhats well known to the assembly.
There were also two thousand people, both those who were still learning and those who had nothing more to learn. Mahāprajāpatī Gautamī, the nun, was there with her retinue of six thousand. Yaśodharā, the mother of Rāhula, the nun, was also there with her retinue.
There were also eighty thousand Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas, all of whom had reached the stage of non-retrogression from Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi (supreme, perfect enlightenment). They all possessed dhāranīs and were gifted in joyful speech and eloquence, turning the Dharma wheel of non-retrogression. They had made offerings to countless hundreds of thousands of Buddhas and planted roots of virtue at their feet, always receiving praise from the Buddhas. They cultivated compassion in their conduct, skillfully entering the wisdom of the Buddhas. They had a thorough understanding of great wisdom and had reached the other shore. Their fame was heard throughout immeasurable worlds, and they were able to save countless hundreds of thousands of sentient beings.
Their names were: Mañjuśrī Bodhisattva, Avalokiteśvara Bodhisattva, Mahāsthāmaprāpta Bodhisattva, Constant-Progress Bodhisattva, Never-Resting Bodhisattva, Jewel-Hand Bodhisattva, Medicine-King Bodhisattva, Valiant-Giver Bodhisattva, Jewel-Moon Bodhisattva, Moon-Light Bodhisattva, Full-Moon Bodhisattva, Great-Might Bodhisattva, Immeasurable-Might Bodhisattva, Transcending-Three-Worlds Bodhisattva, Bhadrapāla Bodhisattva, Maitreya Bodhisattva, Jewel-Accumulation Bodhisattva, Leader Bodhisattva, and others, numbering eighty thousand great Bodhisattvas.
At that time, Śakra, King of the Devas, was there with his retinue of twenty thousand celestial beings. There were also King Moonlight, King All-Fragrance, King Jewel-Light, and the Four Great Heavenly Kings, each with a retinue of ten thousand celestial beings. The Heavenly King of the Pure Abode and the Great Heavenly King of the Pure Abode were there with their retinue of thirty thousand celestial beings. The Brahmā King Śikhin and the Great Brahmā King of Light, rulers of the Saha world, were there with their retinue of twelve thousand celestial beings.
There were eight great Dragon Kings: the Dragon Kings Nanda, Upananda, Sagara, Vāsuki, Takṣaka, Anavatapta, Manasvin, and Utpalaka, each with hundreds of thousands of followers. There were four great Kinnara Kings: Dharma-Kinnara, Wonderful-Dharma-Kinnara, Great-Dharma-Kinnara, and Upholder-of-Dharma-Kinnara, each with hundreds of thousands of followers. There were four great Gandharva Kings: Music-Gandharva, Musical-Sound-Gandharva, Beautiful-Gandharva, and Beautiful-Sound-Gandharva, each with hundreds of thousands of followers. There were four great Asura Kings: Valiant-Asura, Kharaskandha-Asura, Vimalacitra-Asura, and Rāhu-Asura, each with hundreds of thousands of followers. There were four great Garuda Kings: Great-Might-Garuda, Great-Body-Garuda, Great-Fullness-Garuda, and As-You-Wish-Garuda, each with hundreds of thousands of followers.
King Ajātaśatru, the son of Vaidehī, was there with hundreds of thousands of followers. All of them paid homage to the Buddha's feet and then sat down to one side.
At that time, the World-Honored One was surrounded by the four groups of disciples, who were making offerings, showing reverence, respect, and praise. He was expounding a Great Vehicle sutra for the Bodhisattvas, named the Sutra of Innumerable Meanings, which is a teaching for Bodhisattvas and is protected and remembered by the Buddhas.
After the Buddha had finished expounding this sutra, he sat in the lotus posture and entered the samadhi of the station of Innumerable Meanings. His body and mind remained motionless. At that moment, heavenly flowers rained down—maṇḍārava, mahāmaṇḍārava, mañjūṣaka, and mahāmañjūṣaka flowers—scattering upon the Buddha and the great assembly. The entire world of the Buddha shook in six ways.
At that time, the great assembly—monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen, gods, dragons, yakshas, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, non-humans, as well as minor kings and wheel-turning holy kings—experienced a joy they had never known before. With palms joined, they focused their attention entirely on the Buddha.
At that moment, the Buddha released a ray of light from the white hair between his eyebrows, illuminating eighteen thousand worlds in the east, without missing a single one. This light reached down to the Avīci hell and up to the Akaniṣṭha heaven. In this world, the assembly saw all the sentient beings in the six destinies of those lands, and they also saw the Buddhas who were currently present there. They heard the Dharma that those Buddhas were teaching and saw the monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen who were practicing and attaining the Way. They also saw the Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas following the Bodhisattva path through various causes, beliefs, and appearances. They saw Buddhas who had entered parinirvāṇa and saw jeweled stupas of seven treasures erected to house their relics.
At that time, Maitreya Bodhisattva thought: "For what reason is the World-Honored One now displaying this wondrous, supernatural manifestation? The World-Honored One has entered samadhi; this is an inconceivable and rare event. Who should I ask? Who can answer?" He thought again: "Mañjuśrī, the son of the Dharma King, has already served and made offerings to countless Buddhas in the past. He must have seen such a rare sign before. I will ask him now."
At that time, the monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen, and the gods, dragons, and ghost-spirits in the assembly all thought: "This miraculous sign of the Buddha's light—whom should we ask about it now?"
Then, Maitreya Bodhisattva, wishing to resolve his own doubts and observing the thoughts of the four groups of disciples and the gods, dragons, and ghost-spirits in the assembly, asked Mañjuśrī: "For what reason is there this auspicious sign of supernatural power? Why has the Buddha emitted this great light, illuminating eighteen thousand lands in the east and revealing the glorious adornments of those Buddha lands?"
Wishing to repeat this meaning, Maitreya Bodhisattva spoke in a verse, asking:
Mañjuśrī, tell us why,
The Great Teacher, with light so high,
From brows so white, a radiant gleam,
Illuminates all, like a wondrous dream.
With maṇḍārava and mañjūṣaka showers,
And fragrant sandalwood, through all the hours,
Delighting hearts, a gentle breeze,
The ground so pure, with perfect ease.
This world it shakes, in sixfold sway,
The fourfold host, on that blessed day,
Rejoiced as one, with joy profound,
Such peace and bliss, had ne'er been found.

The light that shines, from eyebrows bright,
Upon the east, dispels all night,
Eighteen thousand lands, a golden hue,
From Avīci's depths, to heavens new,
To Akaniṣṭha's highest sphere,
All worlds revealed, so plain and clear.
Six kinds of beings, in life and death's flow,
Their good and evil karma, we now know,
And all rewards, both sweet and sour,
Can all be seen, in this bright hour.

We see the Buddhas, lions of men,
Expounding scriptures, again and again,
Subtle and sublime, their voices pure,
Gentle sounds, that long endure,
Teaching millions, Bodhisattvas bold,
The Brahma sound, a story told,
That makes us yearn, to hear anew,
In their own worlds, the Dharma true,
Explaining causes, with parables grand,
To light the Dharma, throughout the land,
And waken beings, from their slumber deep.

If suffering comes, and sorrows creep,
Despising age, and sickness' sting,
The Buddha preaches, nirvana's spring,
Ending all pain, a sweet release.
If merit's there, and inner peace,
With offerings made, to Buddhas past,
And seeking Dharma, that will last,
The Buddha shows, the Pratyekabuddha's way.
If Buddha's son, from day to day,
Cultivates practices, with wisdom's plea,
The pure path opens, for them to see.

Mañjuśrī, as I stand here,
Such things I see, and hold them dear,
Thousands of millions, now unfold,
A brief account, will now be told.
In those far lands, as Ganges' sand,
Bodhisattvas seek, the Buddha's hand.
Some practice giving, with open heart,
Of gold and silver, a precious part,
Coral and pearls, and mani's gleam,
Tridacna, agate, a shining dream,
Diamonds and jewels, beyond compare,
Slaves and servants, carriages rare,
Jeweled palanquins, with joy they give,
To Buddha's Way, that all may live.
They vow to gain, this vehicle grand,
The foremost one, in every land,
Praised by all Buddhas, in realms above.

Or Bodhisattvas, filled with love,
Give jeweled carriages, with horses four,
With railings bright, and canopies' store,
Adorned with flowers, a lovely sight.
Again I see, with pure delight,
Bodhisattvas giving, flesh and hand,
Their feet, their wives, throughout the land,
Even their children, for the Way so high.
I see them gladly, with upward eye,
Giving their heads, their eyes, their frame,
To seek the Buddha's wisdom, and his name.

Mañjuśrī, I see kings,
To Buddha's place, their spirit brings,
Asking for Way, supreme and grand.
They leave their lands, a pleasant strand,
Palaces, ministers, and consorts dear,
Shave hair and beard, with naught to fear,
And don the robes, of Dharma's call.

Or Bodhisattvas, rising tall,
Become as monks, in quiet space,
Reciting scriptures, with joyful grace.
I see them striving, with might and main,
Entering mountains, to ease all pain,
To contemplate the Buddha's mind.
And those who leave desire behind,
In empty places, quiet and deep,
Cultivating meditation, while others sleep,
Gaining the powers, fivefold and bright.

I see them sitting, bathed in light,
In meditation, with palms so high,
Praising the Kings of Dharma, to the sky,
With millions of verses, a chorus sweet.
Again I see them, with wisdom complete,
With firm resolve, and knowledge deep,
Asking the Buddhas, secrets to keep,
Receiving all, and holding fast.

I see the Buddha's sons, built to last,
In wisdom and samādhi, they excel,
With countless parables, the Dharma they tell,
Delighting in teaching, with grace and might,
Transforming Bodhisattvas, with inner light,
Breaking Māra's armies, with valiant hand,
Beating the Dharma drum, throughout the land.

I see Bodhisattvas, silent and serene,
Revered by gods and dragons, a noble scene,
But not by praise, are they swayed.
I see them shining, in forest glade,
Saving those suffering, in hell's dark night,
Leading them onward, to Buddha's light.

I see the Buddha's sons, who never rest,
Pacing the forest, put to the test,
Diligent seeking, the Buddha's Way.
I see those pure, from day to day,
Flawless in conduct, like jewels so bright,
As they seek the Buddha's guiding light.

I see the Buddha's sons, in patience's power,
Enduring insults, in every hour,
Beatings of arrogant, they bravely face,
As they seek the Buddha's saving grace.

I see Bodhisattvas, from jokes they flee,
And foolish family, to be truly free,
Associating with wise, with single aim,
Removing distractions, and calling His Name,
Collecting thoughts, in mountains and woods,
For millions of years, as true one good,
As they seek the Buddha's perfect Way.

Or I see Bodhisattvas, come what may,
Making offerings, of food so fine,
And medicines diverse, a gift divine,
To Buddhas and Sangha, with hearts so true.
Or precious robes, of every hue,
Worth thousands of millions, beyond all price,
Offered to Buddhas, with sacrifice.
Or millions of kinds, of sandalwood sweet,
And jeweled homes, a vision complete,
And wonderful bedding, for rest and ease,
Offered to Buddhas, to bring them peace.
Pure gardens and forests, with blossoms bright,
Flowing springs, and bathing light,
Offered to Buddhas, with love and care.

These and other gifts, beyond compare,
Cultivate fruit, subtle and grand,
With endless joy, throughout the land,
As they seek the Way, supreme and true.

Or Bodhisattvas, with wisdom's view,
Teach Dharma of stillness, and ending strife,
Giving instructions, to all of life.
Or I see them pondering, dharmas' core,
Seeing not two natures, but one, and no more,
Just like empty space, a truth profound.
Again, I see Buddha's sons, on holy ground,
Whose minds aren't attached, to anything here,
With wisdom wonderful, banishing fear,
They seek the Way, so pure and bright.

Mañjuśrī, there are Bodhisattvas, with all their might,
After Buddha's passing, a solemn time,
Make offerings to relics, in realms sublime.
I see Buddha's sons, with fervent grace,
Building stupas and temples, in every place,
As countless as Ganges' sands, so vast,
Adorning their lands, designed to last.
The jeweled stupas, tall and grand,
Five thousand yojanas, in every land,
And two thousand, in width and in length,
A wonder of beauty, and spiritual strength.

Each stupa and temple, a sight to behold,
A thousand banners and streamers, stories untold,
A jewel net canopy, shining above,
Precious bells ringing, with harmony and love.
Gods, dragons, and spirits, with human kind,
Non-humans as well, with incense entwined,
Flowers and music, offerings so sweet,
Constantly offered, at Buddha's feet.

Mañjuśrī, these sons of the Buddha, so bold,
To offer to relics, a story oft told,
Adorn the stupas and temples, with grace.
The lands naturally, in every place,
Become wondrous and beautiful, beyond compare,
Like the Heavenly Tree King, with flowers so fair,
When its blossoms are fully, in glorious bloom.

When the Buddha emitted, one ray through the gloom,
I and this assembly, saw wonders unfold,
Extraordinary visions, more precious than gold.
The Buddhas' great power, and wisdom so rare,
Emitted one pure ray, to banish all care,
Illuminating lands, beyond our sight.
When we saw this, we felt such delight,
A joy we had never, known before.

Mañjuśrī, son of the Buddha, we implore,
Resolve the doubts, of this assembly's heart.
The fourfold groups, they play their part,
Looking with longing, at you and at me.
For what reason, the World-Honored, you see,
Emitted this light, so pure and bright?
Son of the Buddha, answer tonight,
Resolve our doubts, and bring us great joy.

What benefit is there, what good can employ,
In showing this light, so grand and so vast?
Is it to teach Dharma, that forever will last,
That the Buddha attained, at enlightenment's place?
Or to bestow prophecies, with wisdom and grace?
He showed us the Buddha lands, all jeweled and pure,
And let us see Buddhas, a sight to endure.
This is no small cause, a truth you must know,
Mañjuśrī, you see, the seeds that will grow.
The fourfold groups, dragons, and spirits, so keen,
Are looking to you, to tell what is seen.
So what will you say, with wisdom so deep?
At that time, Mañjuśrī said to Maitreya Bodhisattva-Mahāsattva and the other great beings and noble men: “As I reflect, I believe the World-Honored One is now about to preach the great Dharma, to pour the great Dharma rain, to blow the great Dharma conch, to beat the great Dharma drum, and to expound the great Dharma truth. Noble men, in the past, when I was with other Buddhas, I saw this same auspicious sign. After they emitted this light, they then preached the great Dharma. Therefore, you should know that the Buddha’s manifestation of this light today is also for this reason. He wishes for all sentient beings to hear and know this Dharma which is difficult to believe for the people of this world, and so he reveals this auspicious sign.”
“Noble men, in the past, in immeasurable, boundless, and inconceivable asaṃkhyeya kalpas, there was a Buddha named Sun Moon Lamp Light Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. He expounded the true Dharma, which was excellent in the beginning, excellent in the middle, and excellent in the end. Its meaning was profound and far-reaching, its words were skillful and wonderful, pure, unmixed, and complete in the characteristic of pure conduct. For those seeking to become śrāvakas (voice-hearers), he preached the Dharma of the Four Noble Truths to save them from birth, old age, sickness, and death and lead them to ultimate nirvāṇa. For those seeking to become pratyekabuddhas (self-enlightened ones), he preached the Dharma of the Twelve Links of Dependent Origination. For the Bodhisattvas, he preached the Dharma of the Six Pāramitās to help them attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi and become an All-Knowing One.”
“After him, there was a Buddha also named Sun Moon Lamp Light. Then again, another Buddha also named Sun Moon Lamp Light. In this way, twenty thousand Buddhas all had the same name, Sun Moon Lamp Light, and all shared the same surname, Bharadvaja. Maitreya, you should know that the first and the last of these Buddhas all had the same name, Sun Moon Lamp Light, and were complete in the ten titles of a Buddha. The Dharma they preached was excellent in the beginning, middle, and end. The last of these Buddhas had eight sons before he renounced his home. Their names were: Intention, Good-Intention, Boundless-Intention, Jewel-Intention, Increasing-Intention, Doubt-Removing-Intention, Directed-Intention, and Dharma-Intention. These eight princes were majestic and at ease, each ruling over one of the four continents. When these princes heard that their father had renounced his home and attained Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, they all abandoned their royal positions and also renounced their homes. They all conceived the Mahayana resolve and constantly cultivated pure conduct. They all became Dharma teachers, having already planted roots of goodness under millions of Buddhas.”
“At that time, the Buddha Sun Moon Lamp Light preached a Mahayana sutra named the Sutra of Innumerable Meanings, a Dharma for Bodhisattvas protected and remembered by the Buddhas. After he had finished this sutra, he sat in the lotus posture in the midst of the great assembly and entered the samadhi of the station of Innumerable Meanings. His body and mind remained motionless. At that time, heavenly flowers rained down—maṇḍārava, mahāmaṇḍārava, mañjūṣaka, and mahāmañjūṣaka flowers—scattering upon the Buddha and the great assembly. The entire world of the Buddha shook in six ways. At that time, the great assembly—monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen, gods, dragons, yakshas, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, non-humans, as well as minor kings and wheel-turning holy kings—experienced a joy they had never known before. With palms joined, they focused their attention entirely on the Buddha.”
“At that time, the Tathagata released a ray of light from the white hair between his eyebrows, illuminating eighteen thousand Buddha lands in the east, without missing a single one, just as you see these Buddha lands now. Maitreya, you should know that at that time, there were twenty million Bodhisattvas in the assembly who were eager to hear the Dharma. When these Bodhisattvas saw this light illuminating all the Buddha lands, they felt a joy they had never known before and wished to know the cause of this light. At that time, there was a Bodhisattva named Wonderful Light who had eight hundred disciples. When the Buddha Sun Moon Lamp Light arose from his samadhi, he preached a Mahayana sutra named the Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma, a Dharma for Bodhisattvas protected and remembered by the Buddhas. He remained on his seat for sixty minor kalpas. Those in the assembly who were listening also remained in one place for sixty minor kalpas, their bodies and minds motionless, listening to the Buddha’s teaching as if it were only a moment of a meal. At that time, there was not a single person in the assembly whose body or mind felt any weariness.”
“After the Buddha Sun Moon Lamp Light had finished preaching this sutra for sixty minor kalpas, he declared to the assembly of Brahma, Māra, śramaṇas, Brahmins, gods, humans, and asuras that the Tathagata would enter parinirvāṇa at midnight that very day. At that time, there was a Bodhisattva named Virtue-Store. The Buddha Sun Moon Lamp Light immediately gave him a prophecy, saying to the monks: ‘This Virtue-Store Bodhisattva will soon become a Buddha, with the title Pure-Body Tathagata, Arhat, Samyaksambuddha.’ After the Buddha gave this prophecy, he entered parinirvāṇa at midnight. After the Buddha's passing, Wonderful Light Bodhisattva held and taught the Lotus Sutra for a full eighty minor kalpas. The eight sons of the Buddha Sun Moon Lamp Light all took Wonderful Light as their teacher. Wonderful Light taught and transformed them, making them firm in their resolve for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. After these princes had made offerings to countless hundreds of thousands of millions of Buddhas, they all attained the Buddha Way. The last to become a Buddha was named Burning Lamp. Among the eight hundred disciples of Wonderful Light, there was one named Fame-Seeker, who was attached to gain and honor. Although he read and recited many sutras, he did not understand them well and forgot much, which is why he was called Fame-Seeker. Because this person also planted roots of goodness, he was able to meet countless hundreds of thousands of millions of Buddhas, making offerings to them, showing respect, reverence, and praise.”
“Maitreya, you should know that the Wonderful Light Bodhisattva of that time—was he anyone other than me? I was that Bodhisattva. And the Fame-Seeker Bodhisattva—was he anyone other than you? You were that Bodhisattva. Now that I see this auspicious sign, it is no different from the one I saw before. Therefore, I believe that today the Tathagata is about to preach the Mahayana sutra named the Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma, a Dharma for Bodhisattvas protected and remembered by the Buddhas.”
At that time, Mañjuśrī, wishing to repeat this meaning for the great assembly, spoke in a verse, saying:
In ages past, beyond all count,
A Buddha rose, a sacred fount.
Sun Moon Lamp Light, his name so bright,
He shared the Dharma, shedding light, oh Lord, shedding light.

He saved all beings, vast and wide,
And Bodhisattvas, side by side.
To wisdom's path, he led the way,
To Buddha's truth, in that far day, yeah, in that far day.

Before he left his earthly home,
Eight sons he had, who chose to roam
The path of pure and righteous deed,
Following their Sage, sowing wisdom's seed, hmm, wisdom's seed.

A sutra then, the Buddha taught,
"Innumerable Meanings," deeply sought.
Among the throngs, its truths unfurled,
A guiding light for all the world, for all the world, you see.

When done, he sat in lotus grace,
In samadhi's calm, a sacred space.
"Innumerable Meanings" was its name,
A tranquil state, a holy flame, burning so free.

Then maṇḍārava flowers rained down,
And drums of heaven, without a sound,
Played on their own, a wondrous sign,
Gods, dragons, spirits, all divine, a sweet refrain.

All Buddha-worlds began to shake,
A great tremor for all to take.
From 'tween his brows, a light he sent,
Revealing wonders, heaven-bent, and easing pain.

Eighteen thousand lands to the east,
This light revealed, a glorious feast.
Life and death, karma's hold,
In every being, stories told, deep in the soul.

Some saw the lands, with jewels adorned,
Of lapis lazuli, bright and unhorned.
Crystal clear, a dazzling sight,
By Buddha's wisdom, shining bright, worth more than gold.

Gods and humans, dragons too,
Yakshas, Gandharvas, Kinnaras, a view.
Each to their Buddha, offerings made,
In sacred reverence, unafraid, no need to be blue.

Tathagatas, they then did see,
Who found the Way, in majesty.
Like golden mountains, bodies gleamed,
Subtle, wondrous, as if dreamed, a soulful hue.

A golden image, true and bright,
In pure lapis lazuli, bathed in light.
The World-Honored One, in grand array,
Proclaimed the Dharma, come what may, come what may, my friend.

In Buddha lands, beyond all sum,
Countless śrāvakas had become.
By Buddha's light, we could behold,
Those great assemblies, stories told, until the end.

Some were monks, in mountain's keep,
Pure precepts holding, vows so deep.
Like guarding pearls of priceless worth,
They sought enlightenment on this earth, from dust to grace.

Bodhisattvas, too, I saw,
Practicing giving, 'gainst all law
Of selfish gain, with patience true,
Like Ganges sands, their numbers grew, in that holy place.

And Bodhisattvas, deep in thought,
In meditation, stillness sought.
Their bodies, minds, in quiet repose,
Seeking the Way, where wisdom grows, like a gentle breeze.

Others saw, in nature's core,
All dharmas still, forevermore.
In their own lands, the Dharma preached,
The Buddha Way, they bravely reached, and found their ease.

The fourfold group, with joyful heart,
Saw Sun Moon Lamp Light play his part.
With power vast, a wondrous show,
Their hearts rejoiced, a joyous glow, oh, how they sang.

"What is the cause?" they asked around,
As the Honored One, from trance unbound,
Arose from samadhi, revered by all,
Answering their questions, heeding their call, the sweet bells rang.

He praised Wonderful Light, "World's eye you are,
A trust and refuge, a guiding star.
The Dharma's treasury, you uphold,
Its deepest truths, by you are told," every word so true.

"The Dharma I've preached," he then did say,
"Only you can verify this day."
The World-Honored One, with praises high,
Made Wonderful Light's spirit fly, up to the sky so blue.

Then preached the Lotus, sixty kalpas long,
From his seat he moved not, with Dharma strong.
The subtle Dharma, supreme and grand,
Wonderful Light received, throughout the land, for me and for you.

When Lotus Sutra's words were done,
He spoke to gods and everyone:
"The nature true, of all that be,
I've now explained, for you to see," every single plea.

"At midnight, I'll enter nirvana's rest,
Be diligent, put forth your best.
Buddhas are rare, in kalpas vast,
A billion years, their light can last," eternally.

His Buddha sons, with sorrow deep,
Heard of his passing, then did weep.
"How swiftly goes the Buddha's light!"
They mourned his leaving, in the night, a mournful cry.

The sacred ruler, King of Dharma's grace,
Consoled the throng, in that sad place.
"When I pass on, fear not, nor fret,
A guiding light, you'll surely get," beneath the sky.

"Virtue-Store Bodhisattva, wise and true,
The unconditioned's nature, he sees through.
He'll be a Buddha, Pure-Body named,
And sentient beings, will be reclaimed," by and by.

That night, the Buddha entered peace,
Like fire extinguished, finding ease.
His relics scattered, stupas grand,
Were built in reverence, through the land, for all to revere.

Monks and nuns, like Ganges' sands,
With doubled zeal, through all the lands,
Sought the supreme Way, with fervent mind,
Leaving all earthly ties behind, wiping every tear.

Wonderful Light, that teacher wise,
Upheld the Dharma, in his eyes.
For eighty kalpas, long and vast,
The Lotus Sutra's truths he cast, for all to hear.

The eight princes, by Light converted,
In the supreme Way, were now asserted.
Countless Buddhas, they would see,
A journey long, for eternity, year after year.

To Buddhas all, their offerings made,
The great Way followed, unafraid.
Attaining Buddhahood, one by one,
Their prophecies, their race was run, no need to fear.

The last of gods, in heaven's sphere,
Was Buddha Burning Lamp, so dear.
Leader of sages, saving souls,
Beyond all measure, reaching goals, oh, so very clear.

Wonderful Light, with one disciple there,
Who lazy was, without a care.
Attached to fame, and worldly gain,
Seeking applause, enduring pain, it brings a tear.

Unsatisfied, with praise and might,
He sought out families, day and night.
His studies lost, forgotten, dim,
Understanding little, at their whim, oh dear, oh dear.

Thus, "Fame-Seeker," he was called,
Yet many good deeds, he installed.
Countless Buddhas, he did see,
And offerings made, for all to be, banishing all fear.

He served the Buddhas, followed the Way,
Six pāramitās, through night and day.
Now, Śākyas' Lion, he beholds,
A future Buddha, in stories told, and always near.

Soon, Maitreya, he will be,
Saving beings, for all to see.
Immeasurable numbers, vast and grand,
His loving kindness, through the land, calming every fear.

That lazy one, when Buddha passed,
Was you, whose present life is cast.
And Wonderful Light, that teacher great,
Is now my body, sealed by fate, so hold it dear.

Sun Moon Lamp Light, his sign I saw,
Like this one now, defying law.
Today's own Buddha, I now know,
The Lotus Sutra, he'll bestow, for all to hear.

Today's sign, like the one of old,
Buddhas' skillful means, to be told.
This light emitted, strong and bright,
To realize truth, in purest light, oh, so very clear.

Now, all of you, this truth embrace,
Join palms and wait, with single grace.
The Buddha's Dharma, rain will pour,
To quench the thirst, forevermore, and wipe away each tear.

For those who seek the vehicles three,
If doubt or sorrow, there may be,
The Buddha will remove each trace,
And fill your hearts with boundless grace, year after year.






Chapter 2: Expedient Means
At that time, the World-Honored One calmly arose from his meditation and said to Śāriputra: "The wisdom of the Buddhas is profoundly immeasurable. The gate to this wisdom is difficult to comprehend and difficult to enter. It is something that no śrāvaka or pratyekabuddha can know. Why is this? The Buddha has served and been close to hundreds of thousands of millions of countless Buddhas, fully practicing their immeasurable path. He has progressed with valor and diligence, and his name is heard everywhere. He has perfected a profound and unprecedented Dharma. The teachings he gives are always appropriate, but their intent is difficult to comprehend.
Śāriputra, since I attained Buddhahood, I have used various causes, various parables, and a wide array of teachings and countless expedient means to guide sentient beings, enabling them to leave all attachments. Why is this? The Tathagata's expedient means and wisdom pāramitā (perfection) are all fully complete. Śāriputra, the Tathagata’s wisdom and insight are vast, profound, and far-reaching, immeasurable and unhindered. His powers, fearlessnesses, meditations, liberations, and samadhis have penetrated boundless reaches, and he has perfected all unprecedented Dharmas. Śāriputra, the Tathagata can differentiate and skillfully expound all Dharmas with gentle words that please the hearts of the assembly. Śāriputra, to put it concisely, the Buddha has perfected immeasurable, boundless, and unprecedented Dharmas.”
"Stop, Śāriputra, there is no need to speak further. Why? The most rare and difficult-to-comprehend Dharma that the Buddha has perfected can only be fully exhausted by a Buddha together with another Buddha. This is what is meant by the true nature of all phenomena: their suchness of form, suchness of nature, suchness of substance, suchness of power, suchness of function, suchness of cause, suchness of condition, suchness of effect, suchness of retribution, and suchness of how they are all completely alike from beginning to end."
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
The World Hero, beyond all measure,
Gods and people, a boundless treasure,
No one can know the Buddha's grace,
His power, fearlessness, in every place.
Liberations, samadhis, all his ways,
No one can measure through countless days.
From countless Buddhas, I began to strive,
Practiced all paths, to truly thrive.
This Dharma, profound and subtly spun,
Is hard to grasp for everyone.
For ages long, I walked these roads,
At enlightenment's place, shed all my loads.
The fruit attained, I fully knew,
A karmic reward, both deep and true.
The natures, forms, their meanings deep,
Only I and Buddhas, this secret keep.

This Dharma cannot be displayed,
Its words and forms, still and unswayed.
All other beings, cannot comprehend,
Except for Bodhisattvas, with faith to transcend.
Buddha's disciples, who served with might,
Ended defilements, nearing the light,
Even these souls, though pure and keen,
Are unable to grasp what truly has been.

If Śāriputra, filled the earth,
With all his wisdom, since his birth,
To measure the Buddha's wisdom bright,
He could not grasp a single light.
If ten directions, with him were filled,
And other disciples, all so skilled,
Ten thousand worlds, with them arrayed,
Their wisdom combined, still wouldn't persuade.

Pratyekabuddhas, with minds so clear,
Ended defilements, banishing fear,
Filling ten directions, like a bamboo grove,
If with one mind, for eons they strove,
To think on Buddha's wisdom, true and grand,
They could not know one grain of sand.

Newly resolved Bodhisattvas, a countless throng,
To Buddhas offered, their whole lives long,
Understood meanings, skilled in the lore,
Like rice and hemp, from shore to shore,
Filling ten thousand worlds, with hearts so pure,
If with one mind, their wisdom so sure,
For kalpas vast, like Ganges' sand,
Together they pondered, across the land,
They still could not fathom, the Buddha's great plan.

Non-retrogressing Bodhisattvas, a Ganges' tide,
With single mind, if they thought and tried,
They still could not know, the truth inside.

I tell you now, Śāriputra dear,
This unconditioned, beyond all fear,
Profound and subtle, Dharma's great art,
I've fully attained it, within my heart.
Only I know this form, so deep and wide,
The Buddhas of ten directions, also abide.
Śāriputra, know this truth, my friend,
The words of the Buddhas, never bend.

Have great faith and power, in what Buddha preaches,
The World-Honored One's Dharma, reaches,
After long ages, the truth will emerge,
Like a powerful, undeniable surge.

To śrāvaka's assembly, I now declare,
And those who seek Pratyekabuddha's rare,
From bonds of suffering, I set you free,
And caused you to attain nirvāṇa's decree.
The Buddha uses expedient means, so grand,
To show the three vehicles, across the land.
Sentient beings, attached to their plight,
He guides them to freedom, and endless light.
At that time, among the great assembly, there were twelve hundred śrāvaka arhats who had ended all defilements, such as Ajñāta-Kauṇḍinya and others. Also, monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen who had conceived the mind of a śrāvaka or a pratyekabuddha, each thought to themselves: “For what reason does the World-Honored One so earnestly praise these expedient means, and say that the Dharma the Buddha has attained is so profound and difficult to understand, and that what he has to say is so difficult to grasp, beyond the reach of all śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas? The Buddha teaches the meaning of a single liberation, and we have also attained this Dharma and reached nirvāṇa. Yet now, we do not know what this meaning is leading to.”
At that time, Śāriputra, knowing the doubts in the hearts of the four groups of the assembly and not yet understanding himself, said to the Buddha: “World-Honored One, for what cause and for what reason are you so earnestly praising the first expedient means of the Buddhas, this profound, subtle, and difficult-to-understand Dharma? Since the past, I have never heard such a teaching from the Buddha. Now, the four groups of the assembly are all in doubt. We only wish the World-Honored One would explain this matter. Why does the World-Honored One so earnestly praise this profound, subtle, and difficult-to-understand Dharma?”
At that time, Śāriputra, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
The great sage, the Sun of Wisdom bright,
Has spoken this Dharma, a wondrous light.
He says he's attained, with power and grace,
This inconceivable Dharma, in time and space,
Of powers, fearlessness, Samadhis, and liberation's embrace.
The Dharma he found, where enlightenment shone,
Has never been questioned, by anyone known.
My mind's hard to fathom, a mystery deep,
No one can question the secrets I keep.

Now, unasked, he preaches, a path he has trod,
Praising the journey, with blessings from God.
His wisdom so subtle, a wonder to see,
What all of the Buddhas attain, wild and free.

The arhats who ended defilements' dark hold,
And those who seek nirvana, stories untold,
Are now all entangled in doubt's winding thread,
"Why has the Buddha these words wisely said?"

Those seeking the pratyekabuddha's lone way,
The monks and the nuns, at the close of the day,
The gods and the dragons, ghost-spirits so vast,
And gandharvas, etc., their numbers amassed,
All look at each other, with hesitation's slow pace,
Looking up at the Double-Footed Honored One's face.

"What does this mean?" they all earnestly ask,
"We wish the Buddha would lighten our task."
Among the assembly of śrāvakas, so grand,
The Buddha has said, "I am foremost in this land."

Now, even I, with my wisdom so keen,
Am in doubt, cannot grasp what these words truly mean.
"Is this the ultimate Dharma, so pure and so true?
Or is it the path that we all should pursue?"

The children born from the Buddha's own speech,
Join their palms, looking up, hoping wisdom he'll teach.
"We wish that you'd speak, with your subtle soft tone,
And tell us the truth, to make everything known."

The gods, dragons, and spirits, a countless array,
Their numbers like sands where the Ganges does sway,
And Bodhisattvas, the Buddha Way seek,
Eighty thousand of them, humble and meek.

As well as the kings of a million bright spheres,
Have come to this gathering, calming all fears.
With palms joined and hearts filled with deepest respect,
They wish to hear all of the path, quite complete.
At that time, the Buddha said to Śāriputra: “Stop, stop, there is no need to speak further. If I were to explain this matter, all the gods and people in the world would be shocked and full of doubt.”
Śāriputra again said to the Buddha: “World-Honored One, please speak, please speak. Why? The immeasurable, hundreds of thousands of millions of asaṃkhyeya sentient beings in this assembly have previously seen Buddhas. Their faculties are sharp and their wisdom is clear. When they hear what the Buddha says, they will be able to believe it with reverence.”
At that time, Śāriputra, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
The King of Dharma, the Supreme Honored One,
Please speak, do not worry, your wisdom will stun.
For countless beings in this assembly so vast,
Will believe with reverence, their faith holding fast.
The Buddha again stopped Śāriputra: “If I were to explain this matter, all the gods, humans, and asuras in the world would be shocked and full of doubt. The arrogant monks will fall into a great abyss.”
At that time, the World-Honored One again spoke in verse:
Stop, stop, no more words need be said.
My Dharma is subtle, hard to embed.
The arrogant ones, with their haughty pride,
Will surely not believe, with reverence inside.
At that time, Śāriputra again said to the Buddha: “World-Honored One, please speak, please speak. In this assembly, there are hundreds of thousands of millions like us, who from lifetime to lifetime have been converted by the Buddha. Such people will certainly be able to believe with reverence. For a long night, they will be at peace and receive great benefit.”
At that time, Śāriputra, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
Please preach the Dharma, across the land.
I am the Buddha’s eldest son,
Explain and clarify, when you are done.

In this great gathering, vast and wide,
Are countless beings, with faith inside.
The Buddha has, through lives untold,
Converted these souls, brave and bold.

With single minds, their palms they press,
Awaiting words, the Buddha’s address.
For this assembly, we twelve hundred here,
And seekers of the Way, drawing near,
Please condescend to make it clear.

When these good people hear this lore,
Great joy will fill them, to their core.
At that time, the World-Honored One said to Śāriputra: “Since you have earnestly requested three times, how can I not speak? You should now listen carefully and contemplate it well. I will explain and differentiate it for you.”
When he said this, five thousand people in the assembly—monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen—immediately rose from their seats, paid reverence to the Buddha, and withdrew. Why? Because these people had deep roots of transgression and were arrogant, claiming to have attained what they had not yet attained, and to have realized what they had not yet realized. Having such faults, they did not stay. The World-Honored One remained silent and did not stop them.
At that time, the Buddha said to Śāriputra: “This assembly of mine is no longer filled with twigs and leaves; only the pure, true fruit remains. Śāriputra, it is good that these arrogant people have withdrawn. You should now listen well, for I will speak to you.”
Śāriputra said: “Yes, World-Honored One, we joyfully wish to hear.”
The Buddha said to Śāriputra:
“Such a wonderful Dharma as this is preached by the Buddhas only from time to time, just as the udumbara flower appears only once in a while. Śāriputra, you should believe what the Buddha says, for his words are not empty falsehoods. Śāriputra, the Buddhas preach the Dharma according to what is appropriate, but their intent is difficult to grasp. Why? Because I use countless expedient means, various causes, parables, and words to expound all Dharmas. This Dharma cannot be understood by thinking and distinguishing. Only the Buddhas can know it. Why? Because the World-Honored Buddhas appear in the world for only One Great Purpose.
Śāriputra, what is meant by the World-Honored Buddhas appearing in the world for only One Great Purpose? The World-Honored Buddhas appear in the world to enable sentient beings to open the Buddha's wisdom and insight, so they may become pure. They appear in the world to show sentient beings the Buddha's wisdom and insight. They appear in the world to cause sentient beings to awaken to the Buddha's wisdom and insight. They appear in the world to enable sentient beings to enter into the path of the Buddha's wisdom and insight. Śāriputra, this is what is meant by the Buddhas appearing in the world for One Great Purpose.”
The Buddha said to Śāriputra: “The Tathagatas only teach and convert Bodhisattvas. Everything they do is for a single matter: to show and awaken sentient beings to the Buddha's wisdom and insight. Śāriputra, the Tathagata preaches the Dharma for sentient beings by using only the One Buddha Vehicle; there is no other vehicle, whether two or three. Śāriputra, the Dharma of all the Buddhas in the ten directions is also like this.”
“Śāriputra, the Buddhas of the past used immeasurable, countless expedient means, various causes, parables, and words to expound all Dharmas for sentient beings. This Dharma was all for the sake of the One Buddha Vehicle. When these sentient beings heard the Dharma from the Buddhas, they all ultimately attained All-Knowing Wisdom. Śāriputra, the Buddhas of the future who will appear in the world will also use immeasurable, countless expedient means, various causes, parables, and words to expound all Dharmas for sentient beings. This Dharma will all be for the sake of the One Buddha Vehicle. When these sentient beings hear the Dharma from the Buddhas, they will all ultimately attain All-Knowing Wisdom. Śāriputra, the World-Honored Buddhas in the immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of Buddha lands in the ten directions today, who bring great benefit and peace to sentient beings, these Buddhas also use immeasurable, countless expedient means, various causes, parables, and words to expound all Dharmas for sentient beings. This Dharma is all for the sake of the One Buddha Vehicle. When these sentient beings hear the Dharma from the Buddhas, they all ultimately attain All-Knowing Wisdom. Śāriputra, these Buddhas only teach and convert Bodhisattvas, wishing to show sentient beings the Buddha's wisdom and insight, wishing to awaken sentient beings to the Buddha's wisdom and insight, and wishing to enable sentient beings to enter the Buddha's wisdom and insight. Śāriputra, I am also the same now. I know the various desires of all sentient beings, their deep attachments, and their original nature. I use various causes, parables, and words, and the power of expedient means, to preach the Dharma for them. Śāriputra, all of this is for them to attain the One Buddha Vehicle and All-Knowing Wisdom.”
“Śāriputra, in the worlds of the ten directions, there are not even two vehicles, let alone three. Śāriputra, the Buddhas appear in the five turbid and evil ages: the turbidity of the kalpa, the turbidity of defilements, the turbidity of sentient beings, the turbidity of views, and the turbidity of life. Thus, Śāriputra, during the chaos of the kalpa turbidity, sentient beings are heavily polluted, possess avarice and jealousy, and are filled with unwholesome roots. For this reason, the Buddhas use the power of expedient means to differentiate the One Buddha Vehicle and speak of three. Śāriputra, if my disciples call themselves arhats or pratyekabuddhas, and do not hear or know that the Tathagatas only teach and convert Bodhisattvas, these are not my disciples; they are not arhats, and they are not pratyekabuddhas.”
“Furthermore, Śāriputra, if these monks and nuns claim that they have already attained arhatship, that this is their last body, and that they have reached ultimate nirvāṇa, and they no longer strive to seek Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, you should know that all these people are arrogant. Why? If a monk truly attains arhatship and does not believe in this Dharma, there is no such thing. This is with the exception of after the Buddha’s passing, when there is no Buddha present. Why? After the Buddha’s passing, those who can uphold, read, recite, and comprehend the meaning of these kinds of sutras are rare. If they were to encounter another Buddha, they would immediately become clear about this Dharma. Śāriputra, you must believe, understand, receive, and uphold the words of the Buddha with a single mind. The words of the Tathagatas are not empty falsehoods. There is no other vehicle, only the One Buddha Vehicle.”
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
The monks and nuns with arrogant pride,
The laymen too, with much to hide,
And laywomen who do not believe—
Such four groups, their faults they conceive
Not in themselves, a number grand,
Five thousand strong, across the land.
Their precepts have holes, their leaks run free,
Their flaws they guard with careful glee.
These small-minded ones, they've gone away,
The chaff of the assembly, on that day,
Left by the Buddha's majesty's might,
With little merit, dim their light.
Unworthy they, this Dharma to find,
This gathering now, no twigs to bind,
Only true fruit remains, a pure delight.
Śāriputra, listen with all your might,
To Dharma the Buddhas attained, shining bright.
With expedient means and power untold,
For sentient beings, their truths unfold.
The thoughts in hearts, the paths they pursue,
Desires diverse, and natures new,
Good karma, evil, from lives of the past,
The Buddha knows all, from first to last.
He uses causes, parables, and words,
The power of expedient means, like singing birds,
To make all joyful, free from all strife,
He may speak sūtra, gāthā, and stories of life,
Of past events, and jātaka so grand,
Unprecedented events, throughout the land.
He speaks of causes and conditions, true,
And parables, and geya, and upadeśa too.
For those with dull minds, who small Dharma embrace,
Attached to life's cycle, in this fleeting space,
Who shun the profound, the subtle, and deep,
Of Buddhas immeasurable, while they sleep,
Troubled and confused by suffering's hold,
For these, nirvana's story is told.
This expedient means, I did set it so,
That Buddha's wisdom, they might come to know.
I never said that you all would attain,
Buddhahood's glory, again and again.
The reason I kept silent, you see,
The time had not yet arrived, for thee.
But now is the moment, perfect and clear,
To preach the Great Vehicle, banishing fear.
My ninefold teachings, a sacred art,
Are preached for all beings, from the very start.
But entering the Great Vehicle, the foundation laid,
Which is why this sūtra is now displayed.

There are Buddha's sons, with minds so pure,
Gentle and sharp, their wisdom secure.
Under Buddhas countless, they've trod the way,
Profound and subtle, through night and day.
For these sons of the Buddha, I preach this lore,
This Great Vehicle sūtra, and much, much more.
I give them a prophecy, clear and bold,
That Buddhas they'll be, in ages of old,
Because of deep thought for the Buddha's grace,
And pure precepts cultivated, in every place.
These people, hearing they'll Buddhahood gain,
Are filled with great joy, easing all pain.
The Buddha knows their mental state, so deep,
And preaches the Great Vehicle, while they sleep
If a śrāvaka or Bodhisattva, with keen ear,
Hears the Dharma I preach, banishing fear,
Even a single verse, a profound decree,
They will all certainly Buddhas be.
In Buddha lands of the ten directions wide,
Only the Dharma of One Vehicle can ride.
Not two, nor three, save when the Buddha guides,
Through expedient means, where wisdom hides.
He uses temporary names, a guiding light,
To help sentient beings, with all their might,
To understand the Buddha's wisdom, so grand.
The Buddhas appear for this truth in the land,
For this one true matter, the others aren't real.
The Small Vehicle, I'll never reveal,
To save sentient beings, with its limited scope,
The Buddha himself in the Great Vehicle will cope.
The Dharma he's gained, a magnificent prize,
Adorned with meditation and wisdom's wise eyes,
With this, he saves beings, from suffering's chain,
He's realized the supreme Way, again and again,
The Great Vehicle, Dharma of equality's might.
If I converted just one, with the Small Vehicle's light,
I'd fall into avarice, a terrible plight,
This is something that could not be, by day or by night.
If a person believes and in Buddha takes refuge,
The Tathagata won't deceive them, a sacred deluge,
Nor has he intent of avarice or jealousy's sting,
He cuts off all evil, like a bird on the wing.
Thus, the Buddha in ten directions, so bold,
Is uniquely without fear, stories untold.
I've adorned my body with marks, a radiant gleam,
My light illuminates the world, like a beautiful dream.
Revered by immeasurable beings, far and near,
I preach for them the seal of true nature, so clear.
Śāriputra, know this, my vow from the start,
To cause all beings to be no different from my heart.
Just as I vowed in the past, a sacred decree,
It is now fulfilled, for all to see.
I've converted all beings, with wisdom and grace,
And caused them all to enter the Buddha Way's space.
If I were to meet a being, with a mind so dense,
And teach them only the Buddha Way, without defense,
The ignorant would be confused, deluded and slow,
They wouldn't accept the teaching, they wouldn't know.
I know that these beings, roots of goodness not sown,
Are attached to five desires, like seeds overgrown,
By foolish love blinded, afflicted they are,
Because of their desires, they fall from afar,
Into three evil destinies, a sorrowful plight,
And wander in six realms, enduring all night,
The bitter sufferings, a continuous dread.
They receive a subtle form in the womb, it is said,
From lifetime to lifetime, it always will grow,
With little virtue and merit, a sorrowful show,
Tormented by many sufferings, a ceaseless refrain.
They enter thickets of wrong views, again and again,
Like 'existence' or 'non-existence', a tangled embrace.
Relying on these views, in this fleeting space,
They're complete in sixty-two views, a complex design.
Deeply attached to false dharmas, they intertwine,
Firmly holding on, unable to release,
For thousands of millions of kalpas, without peace,
They don't hear the Buddha's name, a distant sound,
Nor the true Dharma, on hallowed ground.
Such people are difficult to save, it is true.
Therefore, Śāriputra, expedient means I now use for you,
Preaching the path to the end of all pain,
And showing them nirvana, again and again.
Although I preach nirvana, a peaceful art,
This is also not true extinction, from the very start.
All phenomena, from their very first breath,
Have always been still and extinct, even in death.
When a son of the Buddha has practiced the way,
He will become a Buddha in a future day.
I have the power of expedient means, so grand,
And so I reveal the Dharma of three vehicles, across the land.
All World-Honored Ones, with voices clear,
Preach the path of the One Vehicle, banishing fear.
Now, all of you in this assembly so vast,
Should remove all your doubts, let them not last.
The words of the Buddhas are not different, you see,
There is only one, not a second vehicle, for thee.

In countless kalpas, in ages long past,
Immeasurable Buddhas, their number so vast,
Hundreds of thousands of millions of kinds,
Their number incalculable, through all human minds.
These World-Honored Ones, with causes diverse,
And parables, and the power of means to immerse,
Countless expedient means, a wondrous array,
Expounded the nature of all Dharmas, each day.
These World-Honored Ones, with wisdom so deep,
All preached the One Vehicle Dharma, while others would sleep,
Converting immeasurable beings, a guiding light,
And enabling them to enter the Buddha Way, with all their might.
And the great holy masters, with hearts so kind,
Who know the deepest wishes, in every mind,
Of all sentient beings in the world, so wide,
The gods, humans, and creatures, where they reside.
Use different expedient means, a skillful design,
To assist in revealing the ultimate truth, so divine.
If there are any sentient beings, with hearts so true,
Who meet a past Buddha, and their teachings pursue,
If they hear the Dharma, and practice giving's art,
Or uphold the precepts, with a pure and kind heart,
Patience, diligence, meditation's deep grace,
Or wisdom, cultivating blessings, in every place,
These people, with spirits so bright,
Have all already attained the Buddha Way's light.
When the Buddhas have passed away, and their presence is gone,
If a person has a soft and good heart, like the dawn,
These sentient beings, with minds so keen,
Have all already attained the Buddha Way, it would seem.
When the Buddhas have passed away, a sorrowful tear,
If one makes offerings to their relics, holding them dear,
And builds hundreds of millions of stupas, so grand,
Of gold, silver, lapis lazuli, throughout the land,
Tridacna, agate, rose quartz, or crystal beads bright,
And they are purely and widely adorned, a beautiful sight,
Decorating the stupas, with artistic grace.
Or if someone builds stone temples, in a hallowed place,
Or those of sandalwood or agarwood, so sweet,
Or of wood and other materials, at their feet,
Or of brick, tile, and mud, a humble display.
If one is in a wilderness, on a lonely way,
And piles up soil to make a Buddha temple, so small,
Even a child at play, answering truth's call,
Piling up sand to make a Buddha stupa, with glee,
These people, with spirits so joyful and free,
Have all already attained the Buddha Way, you see.
If a person, for the Buddha's sake, with devotion so true,
Erects any kind of image, for all to view,
Carving and sculpting it into a form, so fine,
They have all already attained the Buddha Way divine.
Or if it is made of the seven treasures, a wondrous art,
Of tin, red and white copper, from the very start,
Of white lead and tin, or of iron so strong,
Wood, and mud, where these materials belong,
Or if it is adorned with glue and lacquer, with care,
And made into a Buddha image, beyond compare,
These people, with hearts so pure and so bright,
Have all already attained the Buddha Way's light.
If one uses paint to make a Buddha image, so grand,
With the marks of a hundred blessings, across the land,
Whether they do it themselves or have others do it, so clear,
They have all already attained the Buddha Way, banishing fear.
Even a child at play, with innocent grace,
Who uses grass, wood, or a pen, in this hallowed space,
Or even a fingernail, with a tender touch,
To draw a Buddha image, meaning so much,
These people, gradually accumulate merit's bright glow,
And, becoming complete in great compassion, will know,
They have all already attained the Buddha Way, so grand.
The Buddhas only convert Bodhisattvas, throughout the land,
To save immeasurable beings, from suffering's chain.
If a person at a stupa or temple, again and again,
Or before a jeweled or painted image, so bright,
With flowers, incense, banners, and canopies of light,
Makes a respectful offering, with a heart full of praise.
Or if they have someone play music, through all their days,
Beating drums, blowing conches, a joyful sound,
Or playing flutes, zithers, harps, on hallowed ground,
Lutes, gongs, and cymbals, a melodic embrace,
Such wonderful sounds, filling every space,
All of them held as offerings, with love and with grace.
Or if they sing and praise the Buddha’s virtues, so clear,
With a joyful heart, banishing all fear,
Even with a single small sound, so soft and so low,
They have all already attained the Buddha Way, you know.
If a person, with a distracted mind, without a care,
Offers even a single flower, beyond compare,
To a painted image, with a fleeting thought,
They will gradually see countless Buddhas, bravely fought.
Or if a person bows down, with reverence deep,
Or simply joins their palms, while others sleep,
Or even raises one hand, a simple sign,
Or slightly bows their head, with a touch divine,
And makes this offering to the image, so grand,
They will gradually see immeasurable Buddhas, throughout the land,
And they will attain the supreme Way themselves, so bright,
Widely saving countless beings, with all their might,
And entering unconditioned nirvana, with peaceful release,
Like a fire that goes out when the firewood's at peace.
If a person with a distracted mind, and no more to say,
Enters a stupa or temple, on a sacred way,
And says, “Namo Buddhāya” once, a whispered plea,
They have all already attained the Buddha Way, for all to see.
Of the Buddhas of the past, with their wisdom so vast,
Whether they were in the world or had passed,
If a person heard this Dharma, a truth to embrace,
They have all already attained the Buddha Way, in this hallowed space.
The World-Honored Ones of the future, a countless array,
Whose number is immeasurable, for a future day,
These Tathagatas, with wisdom and grace,
Will also preach the Dharma with expedient means, in every place.
All the Tathagatas, with power so grand,
Use immeasurable expedient means, throughout the land,
To save all sentient beings, from suffering's chain,
And enable them to enter the unconditioned wisdom, again and again.
If one hears this Dharma, with an open heart,
There is not a single one who will not become a Buddha, from the start.
The original vow of the Buddhas is, with solemn decree:
“The Buddha Way that I practice, for all to be,
I wish for all sentient beings, with hearts so pure,
To also attain this same Way, forever secure.”
The future Buddhas, with their wisdom so deep,
Although they will speak of hundreds of thousands, while others sleep,
And millions and countless Dharma gates, a wondrous display,
The truth is for the One Vehicle, lighting the way.
The Buddhas, the Double-Footed Honored Ones, so wise,
Know that all phenomena are always without a fixed nature, before their eyes.
The Buddha seed arises from conditions, a truth to embrace,
And for this reason, they preach the One Vehicle, in every space.
This Dharma dwells in its rightful position, so clear,
And the forms of the world are in a constant state, banishing fear.
Having known this at the place of enlightenment, so bright,
The guide teaches with expedient means, with all their might.
The present Buddhas in the ten directions, so grand,
Who are worshipped by gods and humans, throughout the land,
Their number is like the sands of the Ganges, a countless array,
They appear in the world, at the dawn of each day,
To bring peace and comfort to sentient beings, with grace,
And they also preach this same Dharma, in every place.
They know the first stillness and extinction, a truth to embrace,
But with the power of expedient means, in this hallowed space,
Although they show various paths, with wisdom so deep,
The truth is for the Buddha Vehicle, while others sleep.
They know the various practices of sentient beings, so vast,
The deepest thoughts of their hearts, designed to last,
The karma they have cultivated in the past, so true,
Their desires and diligence, for me and for you,
And the sharpness or dullness of their faculties, so clear.
With various causes, banishing all fear,
Parables, and words, they preach with such grace,
With appropriate expedient means, in every place.
I am also the same now, with a heart so kind,
For the sake of bringing peace to sentient beings, I find,
I use various Dharma gates, with wisdom so deep,
To reveal the Buddha Way, while others sleep.
With the power of my wisdom, so clear and so bright,
I know the nature and desires of sentient beings, with all my might,
And preach the various Dharmas with expedient means, so grand,
To make them all joyful, throughout the land.
Śāriputra, you should know, with my Buddha eye, I see,
The sentient beings of the six realms, for all to be,
They are poor and without blessings and wisdom, a sorrowful plight,
They enter the dangerous road of life and death, with all their might,
And their suffering is continuous and never-ending, so sad.
They are deeply attached to the five desires, making them mad,
Like a yak that loves its tail, a foolish embrace.
By its greedy love, it blinds itself, in this fleeting space,
And is unable to see, with eyes so dim.
They do not seek a powerful Buddha, or a sacred hymn,
Or the Dharma that cuts off suffering, from its very start.
They deeply enter into all wrong views, with a heavy heart.
With suffering, they wish to abandon suffering's pain.
For the sake of these sentient beings, again and again,
I give rise to great compassion, a love so grand.
When I first sat at the place of enlightenment, throughout the land,
I contemplated beneath the tree and also walked, so slow,
For twenty-one days, I thought about this, you know:
"The wisdom I have attained, is subtle and bright,
The very first, shining with all its light.
The faculties of sentient beings are dull, it is true,
They are attached to pleasure and blinded by ignorance, too.
How can these types of beings, so lost and so blind,
Be saved?" I pondered, with a thoughtful mind.
At that time, the Brahma Kings, with reverence deep,
The Heavenly Ruler Śakra, while others would sleep,
The Four Heavenly Kings who guard the world, so grand,
And the Great Lord of the Heavens, throughout the land,
And the rest of the heavenly assembly, a countless array,
Their followers numbering hundreds of thousands, each day,
And millions, respectfully joined their palms, so clear,
And bowed, and asked me to turn the Dharma wheel, banishing fear.
I then thought to myself, with a heavy heart,
"If I only praise the Buddha Vehicle, from the very start,
Sentient beings who are sunk in suffering's deep pain,
Will not be able to believe in this Dharma, again and again.
Because they will not believe and will reject the Dharma, so sad,
They will fall into the three evil destinies, making them mad.
It would be better for me not to preach the Dharma, so clear,
And to quickly enter nirvana," banishing all fear.
I then remembered the Buddhas of the past, with their grace,
And their power of expedient means, in every place.
"The Way that I have now attained, so bright and so free,
I should also preach the three vehicles, for all to see."
When I was thinking this, with a thoughtful mind,
The Buddhas of the ten directions all appeared, so kind.
They comforted me with the sound of Brahma, so clear:
"Well done, Śākyamuni, banishing all fear,
The first of all guides, with wisdom so deep!
You have attained this supreme Dharma, while others sleep.
You also should, like all Buddhas, with grace,
Use the power of expedient means, in every place.
We have all attained the most subtle and foremost Dharma, so bright,
But for the sake of all sentient beings, with all our might,
We differentiate and preach the three vehicles, so grand.
Those with little wisdom delight in the small Dharma, throughout the land,
And do not believe that they can become Buddhas, it is true.
Therefore, with expedient means, for me and for you,
We differentiate and preach the various fruits, so clear.
Although we preach the three vehicles, banishing all fear,
It is only to teach the Bodhisattvas," they said with grace.
Śāriputra, you should know that I heard, in this hallowed space,
The profound and subtle sound of the holy lions, so grand,
And I joyfully said, "Namo Buddhāya!" throughout the land.
I then thought this: "I have come to this turbid and evil age.
What the Buddhas have said, I will also follow and engage,
And practice." Having contemplated this matter, with a thoughtful mind,
I immediately went to Benares, for all to find.
The true nature of all phenomena is still and extinct, it is true,
And cannot be expressed in words, for me and for you.
With the power of expedient means, for them I did preach,
For the five monks, within my reach.
This is called the turning of the Dharma wheel, so grand,
And so there was the sound of nirvana, throughout the land,
And also the distinct names of the arhat, so clear,
And the Dharma and the Sangha, banishing all fear.
From ancient kalpas ago, with wisdom so deep,
I have praised this Dharma of nirvana, while others sleep,
Where the suffering of life and death is completely ended, so bright.
I have always preached in this way, with all my might.
Śāriputra, you should know, I see the sons of the Buddha, so grand,
Those who aspire to the Buddha Way, throughout the land,
Immeasurable millions of them, with hearts so pure,
With respectful hearts, they all come, to the Buddha’s place, secure.
They have previously heard from the Buddhas, with wisdom so deep,
The Dharma that was preached with expedient means, while others sleep.
I then thought: "The reason the Tathagatas appear, it is true,
Is to preach the Buddha’s wisdom, for me and for you.
Now is exactly the time," so clear and so bright.
Śāriputra, you should know that those with dull faculties, with all their might,
And little wisdom, who are attached to forms, and are arrogant, so sad,
Cannot believe in this Dharma, making them mad.
Now, I am joyful and without fear, with a heart so kind,
And in the midst of the Bodhisattvas, for all to find,
I will honestly abandon expedient means, with grace,
And preach only the supreme Way, in this hallowed space.
The Bodhisattvas who hear this Dharma, so clear,
Have already removed all their nets of doubt, banishing all fear.
The twelve hundred arhats, with wisdom so deep,
Will all also become Buddhas, while others sleep.
Just like the style of preaching, so grand,
Of the Buddhas of the three periods, throughout the land,
I am now also like this, with wisdom so bright,
Preaching the undifferentiated Dharma, with all my might.
The appearance of the Buddhas in the world, so rare,
Is very far away and difficult to meet, beyond compare.
Even if they do appear in the world, it is true,
This Dharma is even more difficult to preach, for me and for you.
For immeasurable and countless kalpas, a long, long span,
It is also difficult to hear this Dharma, throughout the land.
And the person who can hear this Dharma, so clear,
Is also very difficult to find, banishing all fear.
It is like the udumbara flower, so rare and so bright,
Which everyone loves, shining with all its light,
Which is rare for gods and humans, it is true,
And appears only once in a while, for me and for you.
Those who hear the Dharma and praise it with joy, so clear,
Even if they utter a single word, banishing all fear,
Are as if they have already made an offering, so grand,
To all the Buddhas of the three periods, throughout the land.
This person is extremely rare, it is true,
More so than the udumbara flower, for me and for you.
You must not have any doubt, with a heart so pure.
I am the King of all Dharmas, forever secure,
And I universally tell all in the great assembly, so grand,
That I only teach and convert the Bodhisattvas, throughout the land,
With the One Vehicle path, so clear and so bright.
There are no śrāvaka disciples, with all their might.
You, Śāriputra, with wisdom so deep,
The śrāvakas and Bodhisattvas, while others sleep,
Should know that this wonderful Dharma, so grand,
Is the secret key of all Buddhas, throughout the land.
In the five turbid and evil ages, with suffering and pain,
Sentient beings only delight in attachment to desires, again and again.
Such kinds of sentient beings, so lost and so blind,
Will ultimately not seek the Buddha Way, for all to find.
The evil people of the coming age, with hearts so cold,
Who hear the Buddha preach the One Vehicle, a story untold,
Will be deluded and will not believe or accept it, so sad,
They will reject the Dharma and fall into evil destinies, making them mad.
For those who have shame and are pure, with a heart so kind,
And aspire to the Buddha Way, for all to find,
For such people, I will widely praise the One Vehicle path, so clear.
Śāriputra, you should know that the Dharma of the Buddhas, banishing all fear,
Is like this. With millions of expedient means, so grand,
They preach the Dharma according to what is appropriate, throughout the land.
Those who are not familiar with the practices, with wisdom so dim,
Are unable to understand this, a sorrowful hymn.
Since you all have now known that the Buddhas are the teachers of the world,
And that these are all matters of expedient means, a story untold,
There will be no more doubts, with hearts so pure.
Your hearts will be filled with great joy, forever secure,
And you will know that you will become Buddhas, with light so bright.

The Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma, Volume Two
Translated by Tripitaka Master Kumarajiva of the Kucha Kingdom in the Later Qin Dynasty, by imperial decree.

Chapter 3: A Parable
At that time, Śāriputra was filled with immense joy. He rose, joined his palms, and, looking up at the World-Honored One’s revered face, said to the Buddha: “Having heard this Dharma sound from the World-Honored One today, my heart is filled with unprecedented joy. Why? In the past, when I heard this Dharma from the Buddha and saw the Bodhisattvas receiving prophecies of their future Buddhahood, I was not included in this, and I felt great sadness, as if I had lost the Tathagata’s immeasurable wisdom and insight.
World-Honored One, I often stayed alone in the mountains, forests, or under trees, whether sitting or walking. I would always think: ‘We have entered the same Dharma nature. Why has the Tathagata saved us with the Small Vehicle Dharma?’ This was our own fault, not the World-Honored One’s. Why? If we had waited for the reason to be revealed and then cultivated to attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, we would have certainly been saved by the Great Vehicle. But we did not understand the Buddha’s expedient means and his teachings according to our capacity. When we first heard the Dharma, we met it, believed in it, and sought to realize it with our minds. World-Honored One, since that time, I have constantly reproached myself, day and night.
But today, from the Buddha, I have heard a Dharma I have never heard before, an unprecedented Dharma, which has cut off all my doubts and regrets. My body and mind are at ease and have found true peace. Today I know that I am truly a son of the Buddha, born from the Buddha’s mouth, transformed by the Dharma, and a sharer in the Buddha’s Dharma.”
At that time, Śāriputra, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
The Dharma's sound, a truth profound,
A treasure gained, where none was found.
My heart now leaps with purest glee,
From doubt's dark net, completely free.
Once taught by Buddha, wisdom deep,
The Great Vehicle, I did not keep.
His voice, so rare, a gentle plea,
From sentient beings, sets burdens free.

My stains are gone, my worries cease,
Upon hearing this, I found release.
In mountain vale, or forest tree,
Whether sitting, or walking free,

I pondered always, this deep thought,
"Alas, myself, how have I fought?
How have I fooled my very soul?"
We're Buddha's sons, to make us whole.

Entered the Dharma, unconditioned, vast,
Yet in the future, could not cast
The supreme Way, for all to hear,
With golden marks, dispelling fear.

The thirty-two, the powers ten,
Liberations for all women and men.
In the same Dharma, we all abide,
Yet this deep truth, we could not guide.

The eighty marks, so subtle, fine,
Eighteen unique, a sacred sign—
All these great merits, I believed,
Were lost to me, and I was grieved.

Walking alone, in quiet grace,
I saw the Buddha, in that space.
His fame did fill the ten directions wide,
Bringing benefit, on every tide.

I thought such gain, I had let fall,
Deceiving truly, beyond recall.
Day and night, I yearned to know,
"Have I lost it, or will it grow?"

I saw the Buddha, day and night,
Praising Bodhisattvas, with all his might.
For this, my thoughts did always turn,
This sacred matter, I sought to learn.

Now hear the Buddha's voice so clear,
The Dharma preached, banishing fear.
Unconditioned, past what mind can trace,
Leading the assembly to wisdom's place.

Once caught in views, a Brahmin guide,
The World-Honored One, my heart inside,
He knew my errors, pulled them free,
And preached nirvana's mystery.

My wrong views gone, no longer bound,
Emptiness' Dharma, I truly found.
At that time, I thought, with deep content,
That final ending, I had sent.

But now I know, with clearer sight,
It was not true extinction's light.
Only when Buddha, I become,
With marks thirty-two, a future sum,

Revered by gods, by humans too,
By yakshas, dragons, spirits new,
Only then can I truly say,
All suffering's ended, come what may.

The Buddha spoke, in assembly grand,
That I'd become Buddha, in this land.
Hearing this Dharma's sacred sound,
All doubts and regrets, no more are found.

When first I heard, what Buddha said,
My heart was shocked, with doubt instead.
"Has a demon come, in Buddha's guise," I thought,
"To trouble my mind, a battle fought?"

The Buddha uses causes, diverse and deep,
With parables, and words to keep
The mind at peace, like ocean wide,
My net of doubt, was cast aside.

The Buddha said, in ages past,
Countless Buddhas, their die was cast.
All dwelled in means, with skillful art,
And preached this Dharma, from the heart.

The Buddhas present, and those to come,
Their number vast, beyond all sum,
Will also use, with skillful hand,
To expound this Dharma, throughout the land.

Just like the Honored One, today,
From birth and leaving, on his way,
To gaining Way, and turning wheel,
He preaches means, for us to feel.

The Honored One, the true Way shows,
Māra would not, as everyone knows.
Because of this, I'm truly sure,
No demon's acting, to obscure.

In doubt's dark net, I once was caught,
And Māra's doing, then I thought.
But hearing Buddha's gentle voice,
Profound, subtle, making me rejoice.

His wide, clear preaching, pure and bright,
My heart is filled with great delight.
My doubts and regrets, forever cease,
In true wisdom, I find my peace.

A Buddha I'll be, beyond all fear,
Revered by gods and humans here,
Turning the wheel, supreme and grand,
To teach Bodhisattvas, throughout the land.
At that time, the Buddha said to Śāriputra: “I now declare in the great assembly of gods, humans, śramaṇas, and brahmins that I once, for the sake of the supreme Way, taught and converted you under two hundred thousand millions of Buddhas. You have also followed me and received my teachings for a long night of existence. I used expedient means to guide you, which is why you were born into my Dharma. Śāriputra, in the past, I taught you to aspire to the Buddha Way, but you have now forgotten it completely and instead thought you had attained extinction. I now wish to make you recall your original vow and the path you have traveled. Therefore, I am preaching this Great Vehicle sutra for the śrāvakas, named the Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma, a Dharma for Bodhisattvas protected and remembered by the Buddhas.”
“Śāriputra, in a future lifetime, after immeasurable, boundless, and inconceivable kalpas, you will make offerings to a great many millions of Buddhas, uphold the true Dharma, and completely practice the path of a Bodhisattva. You will then attain Buddhahood with the title Flower Light Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. His land will be named Stainless, and that land will be level, pure, and beautifully adorned, peaceful, prosperous, and teeming with gods and humans. Its ground will be of lapis lazuli, with eight intersecting roads, and golden ropes will line their sides. Beside them, there will be rows of trees of seven treasures, always bearing flowers and fruits. Flower Light Tathagata will also use the three vehicles to teach and convert sentient beings.”
“Śāriputra, when that Buddha appears, although it will not be in an evil age, he will, due to his original vow, preach the Dharma of the three vehicles. That kalpa will be named Great Jewel Adornment. Why is it named Great Jewel Adornment? Because in that land, the Bodhisattvas are the great jewels. Those Bodhisattvas will be immeasurable, boundless, and inconceivable, beyond the reach of calculation and parables. Only the power of a Buddha’s wisdom can know them. When they wish to walk, precious flowers will support their feet. These Bodhisattvas will not have just begun to conceive the mind. They will have planted roots of virtue long ago, cultivated pure conduct under immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of Buddhas, and always received praise from the Buddhas. They will constantly cultivate the Buddha’s wisdom, be complete in great supernatural powers, and be skilled in knowing the gateways to all Dharmas. They will be simple and honest, without falseness, and their resolve will be firm. Such Bodhisattvas will fill that land.”
“Śāriputra, the life span of Flower Light Buddha will be twelve minor kalpas, not including the time before he was a prince and had not yet become a Buddha. The people in his land will live for eight minor kalpas. After Flower Light Tathagata has been in the world for twelve minor kalpas, he will give a prophecy to the Bodhisattva Firm-Fullness for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. He will tell the monks: ‘This Firm-Fullness Bodhisattva will next become a Buddha, with the title Flower-Foot Peaceful-Practice Tathagata, Arhat, Samyaksambuddha, and his Buddha land will also be like this.’ Śāriputra, after the passing of this Flower Light Buddha, his True Dharma will last for thirty-two minor kalpas, and his Dharma-Image will also last for thirty-two minor kalpas.”
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
Śāriputra, hear my word,
In a future life, a truth inferred.
A Buddha you shall then become,
Of All Wisdom, the Honored One.
