We're caught in that Small Vehicle's weary ways,
Don't know how to reach those enlightened days.

Heard your voice, Lord, said we'd be Buddhas too,
Still got them worries, the blues runnin' through.
Like that hungry soul, can't quite make the start,
'Til prophecy's given, to ease this weary heart.

Oh, great and mighty Buddha, strong and true,
You long for peace, in all that you do.
Please give us that word, Lord, clear and bright,
Like tellin' the hungry, it's time to eat right.
At that time, the World-Honored One, knowing the thoughts in the hearts of his great disciples, said to all the monks: “This Subhūti, in a future lifetime, will serve and see three million million nayuta Buddhas, make offerings to them, show respect, reverence, and praise, and will constantly cultivate pure conduct and be complete in the Bodhisattva Way. In his last body, he will become a Buddha, named Name and Form Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. The kalpa will be named Having-Treasures, and the land will be named Treasure-Born. His land will be level, with a ground of crystal, and jeweled trees will serve as adornments. There will be no hills, pits, sand, rocks, thorns, or filth. Jeweled flowers will cover the ground, and it will be completely pure. The people of his land will all live in jeweled towers and wonderful mansions. The śrāvaka disciples will be immeasurable and boundless, beyond the reach of calculation and parables. The Bodhisattva assemblies will be countless millions of nayuta. The Buddha’s life span will be twelve minor kalpas. The True Dharma will remain in the world for twenty minor kalpas, and the Dharma-Image will also remain for twenty minor kalpas. That Buddha will always dwell in the air and preach the Dharma for the assembly, saving and liberating immeasurable Bodhisattvas and śrāvaka assemblies.”
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
Monks, I tell you true, from me you must hear,
You gotta be of one mind, banish all doubt and fear.
Listen to these words I say, let 'em sink down deep,
Good tidings I bring, secrets you will keep.
My great disciple, Subhūti, soon to be divine,
Attainin' Buddhahood, oh it's a mighty sign.
Name and Form his title, a sound so clear and grand,
Preachin' wisdom's gospel, across every land.

He'll make offerings to Buddhas, countless millions strong,
Walkin' that great Way, where he truly belongs.
Followin' the path they've walked, through joy and through strife,
Bringin' peace to all souls, for eternal life.

His very last body, thirty-two marks he'll claim,
Majestic and wondrous, shoutin' out his name.
Like a jeweled mountain, shinin' in the light,
A beacon for the weary, through the darkest night.

His Buddha land will be, so pure and adorned,
Every soul who sees it, they'll never be scorned.
Love and delight will fill 'em, from their heart's deep core,
Never turnin' away, always wantin' more.

He'll save immeasurable beings, within that blessed place,
In that Buddha's Dharma, full of truth and grace.
Many Bodhisattvas there, with faculties so keen,
Turnin' that great wheel, a holy, righteous scene.

Non-retrogressing they'll be, never lookin' back,
That land always adorned, on the rightest track.
Śrāvaka assemblies, too many to count by far,
Attainin' three wisdoms, shinin' like a star.

Complete in six powers, supernatural and grand,
Dwellin' in eight liberations, across that holy land.
Great majesty and virtue, flowin' all around,
When that Buddha preaches, a sweet and soulful sound.

Supernatural powers, beyond all you can conceive,
Transformations amazin', in what you believe.
Gods and human beings, like Ganges' sands they'll be,
Joinin' their palms together, for all the world to see.

Listenin' to the Buddha's words, every single one,
The life span of that Buddha, 'til his work is done.
Twelve minor kalpas, that's how long he'll stay,
Shinin' his light brightly, every single day.

True Dharma will remain, for twenty kalpas long,
Dharma-Image right beside it, where it truly belongs.
Twenty minor kalpas, for the world to see,
A bluesy, holy lesson, for eternity.
At that time, the World-Honored One again said to the assembly of monks: “I now tell you, this great Mahākātyāyana, in a future lifetime, will use various offerings to serve and make offerings to eight thousand million Buddhas, with reverence and respect. After these Buddhas pass away, he will erect stupas for each of them, a thousand yojanas tall, and five hundred yojanas in both length and width. They will all be made of the seven treasures—gold, silver, lapis lazuli, tridacna, agate, pearls, and rose quartz. He will use all kinds of flowers, garlands, paste incense, powdered incense, burning incense, silken canopies, banners, and streamers to make offerings to the stupas and temples. After this, he will again make offerings to twenty thousand million Buddhas, in the same way. Having made offerings to all these Buddhas, and being complete in the Bodhisattva Way, he will attain Buddhahood, with the title Jambunada Gold Light Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. His land will be level, with a ground of crystal, and jeweled trees will serve as adornments. Golden ropes will line the sides of the roads, and wonderful flowers will cover the ground. It will be completely pure and those who see it will rejoice. There will be no four evil destinies: hells, hungry ghosts, animals, or asuras. There will be many gods, humans, śrāvaka assemblies, and Bodhisattva assemblies, immeasurable millions, to adorn his land. The Buddha's life span will be twelve minor kalpas. The True Dharma will remain in the world for twenty minor kalpas, and the Dharma-Image will also remain for twenty minor kalpas.”
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
Monks, listen close, with a single mind,
What I'm tellin' you, is one of a kind.
This Kātyāyana, with a generous hand,
Will bring fine offerings across the land,
To all the Buddhas, with a joyful heart,
Playin' a faithful and righteous part.
When the Buddhas pass on, from this earthly coil,
He'll build up stupas, from precious soil,
Seven treasures shinin', in the sun's warm glow,
With flowers and incense, watchin' spirits grow.
To the holy relics, he'll bring his praise,
Through all his earthly, and heavenly days.

In his last body, when his time is due,
Buddha's wisdom will shine, bright and true.
A Truly Enlightened, one he will be,
His land pure and peaceful, for all to see.
Millions of beings, he'll save and free,
Worshipped by all, eternally.

The Buddha's light, no one can surpass,
His gentle glow, on every blade of grass.
Jambunada Gold Light, his name will resound,
On sacred ground, where peace can be found.
Bodhisattvas and śrāvakas, their journeys will cease,
Countless and immeasurable, adorning his land with ease.
At that time, the World-Honored One again said to the great assembly: “I now tell you, this great Mahāmaudgalyāyana, will use various offerings to make offerings to eight thousand Buddhas, with reverence and respect. After these Buddhas pass away, he will erect stupas for each of them, a thousand yojanas tall, and five hundred yojanas in both length and width. They will all be made of the seven treasures—gold, silver, lapis lazuli, tridacna, agate, pearls, and rose quartz. He will use all kinds of flowers, garlands, paste incense, powdered incense, burning incense, silken canopies, banners, and streamers to make offerings. After this, he will again make offerings to two million million Buddhas, in the same way. He will then attain Buddhahood, with the title Tāmalapattra Sandalwood Fragrance Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. The kalpa will be named Joy-Full, and the land will be named Pleasure-Wished. His land will be level, with a ground of crystal, and jeweled trees will serve as adornments. Pearls will be scattered as flowers, and it will be completely pure and those who see it will rejoice. There will be many gods, humans, Bodhisattvas, and śrāvakas, whose numbers will be immeasurable. The Buddha’s life span will be twenty-four minor kalpas. The True Dharma will remain in the world for forty minor kalpas, and the Dharma-Image will also remain for forty minor kalpas.”
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
My disciple, now hear what I say,
Great Mahāmaudgalyāyana, after this life's day.
He'll see Buddhas, two million million, standing tall,
For the Dharma's path, he'll give his all.
Under their gaze, pure conduct he'll keep,
Through kalpas uncounted, the Dharma he'll seep.
When the Buddhas pass, seven treasures he'll raise,
Stupas with gold shafts, in a sacred haze.

With flowers and incense, and music so sweet,
He'll honor their temples, from his head to his feet.
Slowly perfecting, the Bodhisattva's grand way,
In Pleasure-Wished land, he'll see his new day.

Tāmalapattra, Sandalwood Fragrance, his name will resound,
Twenty-four kalpas, his life will be found.
Preaching the Dharma, for gods and for man,
Śrāvakas countless, like the Ganges' sand.

With wisdom and power, a majestic array,
Bodhisattvas countless, with firm resolve to stay.
In the Buddha's deep wisdom, they'll never fall back,
After the Buddha's passing, the True Dharma's on track.

For forty minor kalpas, its light will still gleam,
The Dharma-Image shining, like a beautiful dream.
All my disciples, with virtue so grand,
Five hundred in number, prophecies in their hand.

In a lifetime to come, Buddhas they'll all be,
The karmic connections, between you and me.
I'll speak of them now, so listen close, I implore,
Hear the old story, and want for no more.



Chapter 7: A Parable of the Phantom City
The Buddha said to all the monks: "It was in the past, in immeasurable, boundless, and inconceivable asaṃkhyeya kalpas, that there was a Buddha named Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. His land was named Good-City, and the kalpa was named Great-Mark.
Monks, it has been a very long time since that Buddha passed away. It is like if someone were to take all the ground of the three-thousand-great-thousand-fold world, grind it all into ink, and then, after passing a thousand worlds in the east, drop a single dot the size of a tiny grain of dust. Then, after passing another thousand worlds, drop another dot. In this way, he continues until all the ground is used up as ink. What do you think, monks? Can any calculator or student of a calculator figure out the end and know the number of these worlds, or not?"
"No, World-Honored One."
"Monks, the worlds that this person passed, whether they received a dot or not, if they were all ground into dust, and each grain of dust were a kalpa, the time since that Buddha passed away would surpass this number by immeasurable, boundless hundreds of thousands of millions of asaṃkhyeya kalpas. With the power of the Tathagata's wisdom and insight, I see that distant time as if it were today."
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
In ancient days, a long, long time ago,
A Buddha walked, where wisdom's waters flow.
Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom, was his name,
He lit the world with an eternal flame.
Now picture this, a world so vast and grand,
Ground down to dust, held in a mighty hand.
Each speck of dust, it turns to darkest ink,
A cosmic story, on the edge of the brink.
A thousand lands, he travels through the haze,
A single dot, in those ancient, dusty days.
He marks his path, with every tiny spot,
Until the ink, and dust, are all forgot.
The lands all marked, and those untouched by sight,
Are ground to dust, beneath the fading light.
Each tiny grain, a kalpa, deep and old,
A tale of ages, waiting to unfold.
Beyond that count, the kalpas stretch and weave,
Since that old Buddha, took his final leave.
An endless span, a time beyond all thought,
The wisdom deep, that truly he had brought.
The Tathagata, with wisdom pure and free,
He sees that past, for all eternity.
That Buddha's passing, clear as yesterday's sun,
His followers too, when their long race was run.
So listen close, all you who walk this way,
The Buddha's wisdom shines, to this very day.
So pure and subtle, a light that can't be bound,
Through countless kalpas, its truth is ever found.
The Buddha said to all the monks: "The life span of Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Buddha was five hundred and forty million million nayuta kalpas. When that Buddha first sat at the place of enlightenment, after defeating the army of Māra, he was about to attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, but the Dharmas of the Buddhas did not appear before him. In this way, for one minor kalpa, and even up to ten minor kalpas, he sat in the lotus posture, his body and mind motionless, and yet the Dharmas of the Buddhas still did not appear before him."
"At that time, the gods of the Thirty-three Heavens had already prepared a lion's seat for that Buddha under the bodhi tree, a yojana in height. On this seat, the Buddha would attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. As soon as he sat on this seat, all the Brahma Kings rained down various heavenly flowers over a hundred yojanas. A fragrant wind would come from time to time, blowing away the withered flowers and raining down new ones. This continued for ten minor kalpas to make offerings to the Buddha, and even until his passing away, this rain of flowers continued. The Four Heavenly Kings, to make offerings to the Buddha, constantly beat heavenly drums, and the other heavenly beings played heavenly music. This continued for ten minor kalpas, and even until his passing away, it was also like this."
"Monks, when Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Buddha passed ten minor kalpas, the Dharmas of all the Buddhas then appeared before him, and he attained Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. When that Buddha had not yet renounced his home, he had sixteen sons. The first of them was named Wisdom-Accumulation. Each of his sons had various rare and precious playthings. When they heard that their father had attained Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, they all gave up their treasures and went to the Buddha's place. Their mothers followed them, weeping. Their grandfather, a wheel-turning holy king, with a hundred ministers and a hundred thousand million other people, all surrounded them and followed them to the place of enlightenment. They all wished to get close to the Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata, to make offerings to him, to show him reverence, respect, and praise. When they arrived, they bowed their heads at his feet, circled the Buddha a hundred times, and then, with one mind, they joined their palms and looked up at the World-Honored One, speaking in verse:
The World-Honored One, so grand and high,
To save all souls beneath the sky,
Through countless eons, long and deep,
His Buddhahood, he finally did keep.
All his good vows, now they are done,
A mighty feat, for everyone.
This World-Honored One, so hard to find,
Ten minor kalpas, he kept his mind.
His body, hands, and weary feet,
Stayed still and peaceful, oh so sweet.
His mind was calm, no troubled thought,
No scattered chaos, dearly sought.
He found true stillness, deep and wide,
In unconditioned Dharma, he does reside.
Now we all see, with eyes so clear,
The Buddha Way, banishing all fear.
We gained a blessing, strong and true,
We clap our hands, and hail to you.
Folks always burdened, full of pain,
Blind and without a guide, through sun and rain.
They didn't know the way to ease their plight,
Couldn't find liberation, in the darkest night.
For so long, evil destinies grew strong,
And fewer gods sang their joyful song.
From darkness deep, to darker still,
Never heard a Buddha's name, against their will.
But now the Buddha, he has found the light,
A peaceful, unconditioned way, so pure and bright.
We and the spirits, down below and high,
Got the greatest blessing, reaching for the sky.
So we all bow our heads, and humbly pray,
To the supreme Honored One, at the close of day.
At that time, the sixteen princes, having praised the Buddha in verse, requested the World-Honored One to turn the Dharma wheel. They all said: "World-Honored One, when you preach the Dharma, you bring great peace, compassion, and benefit to the gods and humans." They spoke again in verse:
The World Hero, ain't no equal, it's true,
Adorned with blessings, a hundred or two.
Supreme wisdom, he done surely attained,
We wish you'd preach, let your wisdom be rained.
To save and liberate, us from this plight,
And all sentient beings, in the day and the night.
Please differentiate, reveal it for all to see,
So we can reach that wisdom, set our spirits free.
If we find Buddhahood, all souls will align,
The World-Honored One, knows what's deep in the mind.
He knows the paths they walk, through shadows and light,
And the power of their wisdom, burning ever so bright.
Their desires and pleasures, their blessings they sow,
And the karma they've gathered, from lives long ago.
The World-Honored One, he knows every single thing,
So turn that supreme wheel, let the sweet dharma sing.
The Buddha said to all the monks: "When Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Buddha attained Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, the five hundred million million Buddha worlds in each of the ten directions shook in six ways. The dark, remote places in between these lands, which the light and majesty of the sun and moon could not reach, were all brightly illuminated. The sentient beings within them were able to see one another and all said: 'How is it that sentient beings have suddenly appeared here?' And the heavenly palaces in their lands, and even the Brahma palaces, all shook in six ways. A great light universally shone, filling all the worlds, surpassing the light of the gods."
"At that time, in the eastern five hundred million million worlds, the Brahma palaces shone with a light that was double their usual brightness. The Brahma Kings all thought: 'The light of our palaces is something we have never had before. For what reason is this sign appearing?' At that time, all the Brahma Kings went to each other and discussed this matter. In their assembly, there was a great Brahma King named Savior-of-All, who spoke to the assembly of Brahmas in verse, saying:
A light shines bright in every hall,
A sight we've never seen before at all.
We gotta find out, what's the reason why,
Let's search together, beneath this mystic sky.
Has a great and virtuous god come into being?
Or a Buddha appeared, for all the world's seeing?
This mighty light, it shines so far and wide,
Ten directions bathed, with nowhere left to hide.
At that time, the five hundred million million Brahma Kings of those lands, together with their palaces, each filled their robes with heavenly flowers and went to the west to search for the cause of this sign. They saw Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata at the place of enlightenment, under the bodhi tree, sitting on a lion's seat. He was revered and surrounded by gods, dragon kings, gandharvas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, non-humans, and others. They also saw the sixteen princes requesting the Buddha to turn the Dharma wheel.
The Brahma Kings immediately bowed their heads at the Buddha's feet, circled him a hundred thousand times, and then scattered heavenly flowers upon the Buddha. The flowers they scattered were as numerous as Mount Sumeru. They also made offerings to the Buddha's bodhi tree, which was ten yojanas high. After offering the flowers, they each offered their palaces to that Buddha and said: "Please have compassion and benefit us. We wish that you would accept the palaces we have offered." At that time, the Brahma Kings, in the presence of the Buddha, with a single mind and voice, spoke in verse:
World-Honored One, you're a sight so rare,
Hard to find, beyond compare.
Got that boundless merit, true and deep,
Watchin' over all, my soul to keep.
Teacher of gods and humans, great and grand,
Compassion for this weary land.
Every soul, from east to west,
Receives your favor, puts 'em to the test.
We came from lands, a million miles away,
Left sweet meditation, couldn't stay.
Gotta bring our offerings, reverent and low,
To the Buddha, watchin' our spirits grow.
Our palaces, built on blessings from old,
Shinin' bright, a story untold.
Now we lay 'em down, for you to see,
World-Honored One, accept 'em compassionately.
At that time, the Brahma Kings, having praised the Buddha in verse, each said: "We only wish that the World-Honored One would turn the Dharma wheel, to save and liberate all sentient beings and open the way to nirvana." The Brahma Kings, with a single mind and voice, spoke in verse:
World Hero, Honored One, so true,
We only wish you'd share the Dharma, new.
With great compassion, hear our plea,
Save all who suffer, set them free.
At that time, Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata silently gave his permission.
"Furthermore, monks, in the southeastern five hundred million million worlds, the great Brahma Kings each saw their own palaces shining with a light they had never had before. They were overjoyed and filled with a rare feeling. They immediately went to each other and discussed this matter. In their assembly, there was a great Brahma King named Great Compassion, who spoke to the assembly of Brahmas in verse, saying:
Tell me, why's this light shinin' so bright?
Never seen such glory in the dark of night.
Is some great, virtuous god been born anew,
Or a Buddha appeared, for me and for you?
This sign, it's a mystery, a sight so grand,
Gotta search for the meaning, across the whole land.
Through ten million worlds, we'll follow the gleam,
Walkin' and searchin', like in a sweet dream.
Yeah, most likely a Buddha, has come down to earth,
To save all the sufferin' and give new birth.
At that time, the five hundred million million Brahma Kings, together with their palaces, each filled their robes with heavenly flowers and went to the northwest to search for the cause of this sign. They saw Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata at the place of enlightenment, under the bodhi tree, sitting on a lion's seat. He was revered and surrounded by gods, dragon kings, gandharvas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, non-humans, and others. They also saw the sixteen princes requesting the Buddha to turn the Dharma wheel.
The Brahma Kings then bowed their heads at the Buddha's feet, circled him a hundred thousand times, and then scattered heavenly flowers upon the Buddha. The flowers they scattered were as numerous as Mount Sumeru. They also made offerings to the Buddha's bodhi tree. After offering the flowers, they each offered their palaces to that Buddha and said: "Please have compassion and benefit us. We wish that you would accept the palaces we have offered." At that time, the Brahma Kings, in the presence of the Buddha, with a single mind and voice, spoke in verse:
Holy master, king of all gods, yeah,
Voice like the kalaviṅka bird, singin' soft and low.
You got compassion for all us weary souls, Lord,
Now we bow down to you, payin' homage, lettin' our praises flow.
Oh, the World-Honored One, so mighty rare,
He just shows up once in a great, great while.
Hundred and eighty kalpas just passed on by,
Empty as a broken dream, with no Buddha to make us smile.
Three evil destinies, they were overflowin',
And the angels in heaven, their numbers were goin' down.
But now the Buddha's come to this troubled ol' world,
To be the light in the darkness, the eye for every lost and lonesome town.
You're the refuge for this weary ol' world, Lord,
You save and you protect, come what may.
You're the father of all us strugglin' souls,
Got that compassion, bringin' blessings every single day.
From the good times in our lives, way back in the past,
That's why we're here today, feelin' strong and true.
Able to meet the World-Honored One, yeah,
Singin' these blues of gratitude, just for you.
At that time, the Brahma Kings, having praised the Buddha in verse, each said: "We only wish that the World-Honored One, out of compassion for all, would turn the Dharma wheel and save sentient beings." The Brahma Kings, with a single mind and voice, spoke in verse:
Great sage, turn that Dharma wheel, yeah,
And show us the true nature, so clear.
Save these suffering souls, lost and down,
Bring 'em great joy, all over this town.
When folks hear this Dharma, hear what I say,
They'll find the Way, or reach heaven someday.
Bad times gonna lessen, you just wait and see,
Goodness and patience, gonna grow strong and free.
At that time, Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata silently gave his permission.
"Furthermore, monks, in the southern five hundred million million worlds, the great Brahma Kings each saw their own palaces shining with a light they had never had before. They were overjoyed and filled with a rare feeling. They immediately went to each other and discussed this matter: 'For what reason do our palaces have this light?' In their assembly, there was a great Brahma King named Wonderful-Dharma, who spoke to the assembly of Brahmas in verse, saying:
The light in all our palaces, oh, it shines so bright and grand,
A majestic and brilliant glow, across this weary land.
This ain't without a reason, no, a cause we ought to find,
Gotta search for why this sign is here, and leave no truth behind.
For more than a hundred thousand years, this ain't a sight we've known,
Never seen this sign before, on a path we've always sown.
Is a great and virtuous god born, come to ease our troubled mind?
Or has a Buddha appeared in the world, the lost and weary to find?
At that time, the five hundred million million Brahma Kings, together with their palaces, each filled their robes with heavenly flowers and went to the north to search for the cause of this sign. They saw Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata at the place of enlightenment, under the bodhi tree, sitting on a lion's seat. He was revered and surrounded by gods, dragon kings, gandharvas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, non-humans, and others. They also saw the sixteen princes requesting the Buddha to turn the Dharma wheel.
The Brahma Kings then bowed their heads at the Buddha's feet, circled him a hundred thousand times, and then scattered heavenly flowers upon the Buddha. The flowers they scattered were as numerous as Mount Sumeru. They also made offerings to the Buddha's bodhi tree. After offering the flowers, they each offered their palaces to that Buddha and said: "Please have compassion and benefit us. We wish that you would accept the palaces we have offered." At that time, the Brahma Kings, in the presence of the Buddha, with a single mind and voice, spoke in verse:
The World-Honored One, so hard to find,
Breaks through the troubles of every kind.
After a long, long time, we finally see,
His wisdom shines for you and me.
He fills the hungry, he fills the dry,
With the Dharma rain from up on high.
Never seen such a man, so wise and deep,
Secrets of the ages, he does keep.
Like the udumbara, rare and true,
Today, our encounter, fresh and new.
Light in our palaces, a golden gleam,
Living out this wonderful dream.
World-Honored One, your heart's so grand,
Just wish you'd take us by the hand.
At that time, the Brahma Kings, having praised the Buddha in verse, each said: "We only wish that the World-Honored One would turn the Dharma wheel, so that all the world, gods, Māra, Brahmā, śramaṇas, and brahmins may all gain peace and be liberated." The Brahma Kings, with a single mind and voice, spoke in verse:
We only wish the Honored One, of gods and humans too,
Would turn that supreme Dharma wheel, and see us all anew.
Beat that great Dharma drum, let the rhythm fill the air,
And blow that great Dharma conch, chasing away our care.
Universally pour that great Dharma rain, let it wash away the pain,
And save immeasurable sentient beings, again and again.
We all bow and request you, with a heartfelt, soulful plea,
To expound a profound and far-reaching sound, and set our spirits free.
At that time, Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata silently gave his permission. The Brahma Kings from the southwest, and all the way to the nadir, were also like this.
At that time, the five hundred million million Brahma Kings of the zenith also saw their palaces shining with a majestic and brilliant light they had never had before. They were overjoyed and filled with a rare feeling. They immediately went to each other and discussed this matter: "For what reason do our palaces have this light?" In their assembly, there was a great Brahma King named Śikhin, who spoke to the assembly of Brahmas in verse, saying:
Oh, why do our grand halls now shine so bright,
With a glory we ain't ever seen, day or night?
Such a majestic glow, a brilliant sheen,
A wonder in this world, if you know what I mean.
This wondrous sign, it just ain't right,
Never heard a whisper, never seen such a light.
Has a great, good God now come to birth,
Or a Buddha's sweet presence graced this earth?
At that time, the five hundred million million Brahma Kings, together with their palaces, each filled their robes with heavenly flowers and went to the nadir to search for the cause of this sign. They saw Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata at the place of enlightenment, under the bodhi tree, sitting on a lion's seat. He was revered and surrounded by gods, dragon kings, gandharvas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, non-humans, and others. They also saw the sixteen princes requesting the Buddha to turn the Dharma wheel.
The Brahma Kings then bowed their heads at the Buddha's feet, circled him a hundred thousand times, and then scattered heavenly flowers upon the Buddha. The flowers they scattered were as numerous as Mount Sumeru. They also made offerings to the Buddha's bodhi tree. After offering the flowers, they each offered their palaces to that Buddha and said: "Please have compassion and benefit us. We wish that you would accept the palaces we have offered." At that time, the Brahma Kings, in the presence of the Buddha, with a single mind and voice, spoke in verse:
It's good to see the Buddhas, saviors of the world, so true,
Gonna save all us sentient beings, from these three realms, me and you.
The wise and honored One, of gods and humans too,
Got compassion for all creatures, gonna see us through.
Open up that sweet dew gate, let it flow so wide,
Gonna save us all, ain't nowhere to hide.
Past so many kalpas, passed without a sound,
No Buddha in this world, just darkness all around.
Three evil destinies risin', asuras too,
Gods were gettin' smaller, didn't know what to do.
Most folks went down bad roads, when their time was through.
Didn't hear the Dharma, just did unwholesome deeds,
Lost their strength and wisdom, planted sorrowful seeds.
Sinful karma's burden, happiness took flight,
Wrong views held 'em captive, lost in the dark of night.
Didn't know no goodness, couldn't find the light.
No Buddha to convert 'em, just fell to evil's sway,
But the Buddha's the eye of the world, shines a long, long day.
Out of pure compassion, he steps into this strife,
Found true enlightenment, gonna save every life.
Oh, we're so joyful, filled with brand new life.
All the other assemblies, they rejoice and praise,
For this light that's shinin', through these long, dark days.
Our palaces are adorned, with this light so grand,
Offer them to the World-Honored One, with a blessin' hand.
Just wish you'd accept 'em, across this weary land.
May this merit reach all beings, from shore to distant shore,
May we and all creation, walk the Buddha Way, and nothing more.
At that time, the five hundred million million Brahma Kings, having praised the Buddha in verse, each said to the Buddha: "We only wish that the World-Honored One would turn the Dharma wheel, to bring great peace and to liberate many." The Brahma Kings then spoke in verse:
World-Honored One, turn the Dharma wheel,
Beat the Dharma drum of sweet dew,
Save the suffering and afflicted sentient beings,
And reveal the Way to nirvana.
We only wish that you would accept our request,
And with your great and subtle voice,
Out of compassion, expound
The Dharma that you have gathered for immeasurable kalpas.
At that time, Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Tathagata accepted the request of the Brahma Kings of the ten directions and the sixteen princes. He then, in three ways, turned the twelve-linked Dharma wheel—which no śramaṇa, Brahmin, god, demon, Brahmā, or anyone in the world could turn. He taught that "This is suffering, this is the accumulation of suffering, this is the extinction of suffering, and this is the Way to the extinction of suffering." And he widely preached the Dharma of the Twelve Links of Dependent Origination: "From ignorance comes volitional formations; from volitional formations comes consciousness; from consciousness comes name and form; from name and form comes the six sense faculties; from the six sense faculties comes contact; from contact comes sensation; from sensation comes craving; from craving comes grasping; from grasping comes existence; from existence comes birth; from birth comes old age, death, sorrow, grief, suffering, and affliction. When ignorance is extinguished, volitional formations are extinguished; when volitional formations are extinguished, consciousness is extinguished; when consciousness is extinguished, name and form are extinguished; when name and form are extinguished, the six sense faculties are extinguished; when the six sense faculties are extinguished, contact is extinguished; when contact is extinguished, sensation is extinguished; when sensation is extinguished, craving is extinguished; when craving is extinguished, grasping is extinguished; when grasping is extinguished, existence is extinguished; when existence is extinguished, birth is extinguished; when birth is extinguished, old age, death, sorrow, grief, and suffering are all extinguished."
When the Buddha preached this Dharma in the midst of the assembly of gods and humans, six hundred million million nayuta people, because they did not accept any conditioned phenomena, had their minds liberated from all defilements. They all attained profound and subtle meditation, the three wisdoms, and the six supernatural powers, and were complete in the eight liberations. When he preached for the second, third, and fourth time, tens of millions of millions of sentient beings, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges and as many as nayutas, also had their minds liberated from all defilements because they did not accept any conditioned phenomena. From this time on, the assemblies of śrāvakas were immeasurable and boundless, beyond calculation.
At that time, the sixteen princes all renounced their homes as youths and became śrāmaṇeras (novice monks). Their faculties were sharp and their wisdom was clear. They had previously made offerings to hundreds of thousands of millions of Buddhas, had cultivated pure conduct, and were seeking Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. Together, they said to the Buddha: “World-Honored One, these immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of great śrāvakas have all attained their goal. World-Honored One, you should also preach the Dharma of Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi for us. When we have heard it, we will all cultivate and learn it together. World-Honored One, we aspire to the Tathagata’s wisdom and insight. Our deepest thoughts are known by the Buddha himself.” At that time, among the multitude that the wheel-turning holy king led, eighty million people saw the sixteen princes renounce their homes and also asked to do so. The king immediately gave his permission.
At that time, that Buddha accepted the request of the śrāmaṇeras. After two hundred thousand kalpas, he then preached this Great Vehicle sutra in the midst of the four groups of the assembly, named the Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma, a Dharma for Bodhisattvas protected and remembered by the Buddhas. When he had finished this sutra, the sixteen śrāmaṇeras, for the sake of Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, all received, upheld, recited, and mastered it.
While this sutra was being preached, the sixteen Bodhisattva śrāmaṇeras all believed and accepted it, and among the śrāvaka assembly, some also believed and understood. The rest of the sentient beings, numbering millions of millions, all gave rise to doubt. The Buddha preached this sutra for eight thousand kalpas without ever resting. When he finished this sutra, he immediately entered a quiet room and dwelt in meditation for eighty-four thousand kalpas. At that time, the sixteen Bodhisattva śrāmaṇeras, knowing that the Buddha had entered the room and was dwelling in meditation, each ascended a Dharma seat. They also, for eighty-four thousand kalpas, widely expounded and differentiated the Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma for the four groups of the assembly. Each of them saved and converted six hundred million million sentient beings, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, teaching, guiding, benefiting, and filling them with joy, and causing them to conceive the mind of Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi.
When Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom Buddha passed eighty-four thousand kalpas, he arose from his samadhi. He went to the Dharma seat and sat down calmly. He universally announced to the great assembly: “These sixteen Bodhisattva śrāmaṇeras are truly rare. Their faculties are sharp and their wisdom is clear. They have previously made offerings to immeasurable millions and hundreds of thousands of millions of Buddhas. Under all these Buddhas, they have constantly cultivated pure conduct, received and upheld the Buddha’s wisdom, and revealed it to sentient beings, causing them to enter it. You should all constantly be close to them and make offerings to them. Why? If a śrāvaka, a pratyekabuddha, or a Bodhisattva is able to believe in and accept the Dharma preached by these sixteen Bodhisattvas and uphold it without destroying it, this person will all attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi and the wisdom of the Tathagata.”
The Buddha said to all the monks: “These sixteen Bodhisattvas always delight in preaching this Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma. Each of these Bodhisattvas converted six hundred million million sentient beings, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges. In every lifetime, they were born with the Bodhisattvas, heard the Dharma from them, and all believed and understood. Because of this cause, they were able to encounter four million million World-Honored Buddhas, and this will not come to an end in this lifetime.”
“Monks, I now tell you, those sixteen śrāmaṇeras who were disciples of that Buddha have all now attained Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi and are currently preaching the Dharma in the lands of the ten directions. They have immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of Bodhisattvas and śrāvakas as their retinues. The two śrāmaṇeras in the east have become Buddhas; one is named Akshobhya, in the land of Joy, and the other is named Sumeru-Peak. In the southeast are two Buddhas; one is named Lion-Sound, and the other is named Lion-Form. In the south are two Buddhas; one is named Dwelling-in-Space, and the other is named Constant-Extinction. In the southwest are two Buddhas; one is named King-Form, and the other is named Brahmā-Form. In the west are two Buddhas; one is named Amitābha, and the other is named Savior-of-All-Worldly-Sufferings. In the northwest are two Buddhas; one is named Tāmalapattra-Sandalwood-Fragrance Supernatural-Power, and the other is named Sumeru-Form. In the north are two Buddhas; one is named Cloud-Sovereign, and the other is named Cloud-Sovereign-King. The Buddha in the northeast is named Destroyer-of-All-Worldly-Fears. The sixteenth is myself, Śākyamuni Buddha, who has attained Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi in this Saha land.”
“Monks, when we were śrāmaṇeras, we each converted immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of sentient beings, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, for the sake of Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. Some of these sentient beings are now dwelling on the śrāvaka ground. I always teach them Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. These people should gradually enter the Buddha Way with this Dharma. Why? Because the Tathagata’s wisdom is difficult to believe and difficult to comprehend. The sentient beings, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, who were converted at that time, are all of you monks and the śrāvaka disciples in the future after my passing away. After my passing away, there will be other disciples who do not hear this sutra and do not know or realize the practices of a Bodhisattva. They will think of the merits they have attained as extinction and will enter nirvana. I will then become a Buddha in another land, with a different name. These people, although they think they have attained extinction and have entered nirvana, will, in that land, seek the Buddha’s wisdom and hear this sutra. It is only with the One Buddha Vehicle that they will attain extinction; there is no other vehicle, except when the Tathagatas preach with expedient means.”
“Monks, if the Tathagata knows that the time of his nirvana is approaching, and the assembly is pure, their belief and understanding are firm, they have realized the Dharma of emptiness, and have entered deep meditation, he then gathers the Bodhisattvas and the śrāvaka assemblies and preaches this sutra. In the world, there are no two vehicles that can attain extinction, only the One Buddha Vehicle can attain extinction. Monks, you should know that the Tathagata, with his expedient means, deeply penetrates the nature of sentient beings. If they delight in the small Dharma and are deeply attached to the five desires, for the sake of these people, he preaches nirvana. When these people hear it, they will then believe and accept it.”
The Parable of the Phantom City (Prose)
“Imagine a difficult and dangerous evil road of five hundred yojanas, a desolate and uninhabited place of fear. If there is a great multitude who wishes to pass through this road to reach a place of treasures, there is a guide who is intelligent and wise, and who skillfully knows the dangerous road and its open and blocked passages. He leads the multitude, wishing to pass through this danger.
In the middle of the journey, the multitude becomes weary and wants to turn back. They say to the guide: ‘We are exhausted and also afraid, and we cannot go on. The road ahead is still far, and we wish to turn back.’ The guide, who has many expedient means, thinks to himself: ‘These people are pitiful. How can they abandon the great treasures and want to turn back?’ Having thought this, he uses the power of his expedient means and creates a phantom city in the dangerous road, at the distance of three hundred yojanas. He tells the multitude: ‘You should not be afraid or turn back. You can stop and rest in this great city. You can do whatever you wish. When you enter this city, you will be at ease and peaceful. If you can go on to the treasure place, you can also leave.’
At that time, the exhausted multitude was filled with great joy and praised this as something they had never had. ‘We have now escaped this evil road and have gained peace and comfort.’ The multitude then went into the phantom city, and they thought they had been saved and had found peace. At that time, the guide, knowing that these people had rested and were no longer weary, extinguished the phantom city and said to the multitude: ‘You should go on now! The treasure place is near. The great city you just saw was created by me as a place to rest.’”
The Buddha’s Application of the Parable
“Monks, the Tathagata is also like this. I am now your great guide. I know that the evil path of life, death, and afflictions is dangerous, difficult, and long, and should be left and transcended. If sentient beings only heard about the One Buddha Vehicle, they would not want to see the Buddha or be close to him, and would think: ‘The Buddha Way is long and far, and one can only attain it after a long time of diligence and suffering.’ The Buddha knows this timid and lowly mindset and, with the power of expedient means, for the sake of giving them a place to rest in the middle of the path, he preaches the two nirvanas. When sentient beings dwell on the two grounds, the Tathagata then tells them: ‘What you have done is not yet complete. The ground you dwell on is near the Buddha’s wisdom. You should observe and weigh that the nirvana you have attained is not the true one. It is only the power of the Tathagata’s expedient means that, for the sake of the One Buddha Vehicle, differentiates and speaks of three.’ It is like that guide who, for the sake of a rest, creates a phantom city. When he knows they are rested, he tells them: ‘The treasure place is near. This city is not real; I created it for you.’”
The Parable of the Phantom City (Verse)
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
The Buddha Great-Thoroughly-Triumphant-Wisdom,
Sat for ten kalpas, but his light grew dim.
The Dharmas didn't shine, the Way he couldn't find,
Just darkness on his soul and trouble on his mind.

All the gods and spirits, dragon kings so grand,
Asura assemblies, a heavenly band.
They rained down pretty flowers, a sweet, soft, falling dew,
To that struggling Buddha, they made their offerings true.

The gods they beat their drums, a rhythm deep and low,
Played all kinds of music, watched the fragrant breezes blow.
Withered flowers flew away, new ones started to appear,
Chasin' out the shadows, banishin' all fear.

After ten long kalpas, he finally found his stride,
Attained the Buddha Way, with nowhere left to hide.
The hearts of gods and people, they all began to sing,
Filled with joy and delight, the happiness it did bring.

That Buddha had sixteen sons, all with their retinue,
Millions upon millions, saw his wisdom shining through.
They bowed down at his feet, in a humble, hopeful plea,
"Turn the Dharma wheel, set our spirits free."

"May the Dharma rain, from the holy lion fall,
Satisfy our hunger, answer every call.
World-Honored One, so hard to meet, a rare and precious sight,
To awaken all livin' beings, you shake 'em with your light."

In the eastern worlds, five hundred million deep,
The Brahma palaces shone, secrets they did keep.
A light they'd never witnessed, blazing, bright and bold,
A story for the ages, forever to be told.

When the Brahmas saw that sign, they hurried to his place,
Scattered pretty flowers, with smiles upon their face.
They offered up their palaces, with devotion strong and true,
"Turn the Dharma wheel, there's so much work to do."

They praised him with their verses, a sweet and soulful sound,
But the Buddha knew the time, was not yet to be found.
He accepted their request, then sat in silence deep,
While the sacred mysteries, he still had left to keep.

Three directions, four diagonals, above and down below,
They scattered all their flowers, watched the offerings flow.
"World-Honored One, so hard to meet, your wisdom we embrace,
With your great compassion, please show us saving grace."

"Open up the gate of sweet dew, let your mercy pour,"
"Turn the supreme Dharma wheel, we can't ask for much more."
The World-Honored One, with wisdom deep and vast,
Accepted that assembly's plea, a love that's built to last.

He preached the various Dharmas, a lesson clear and plain,
The Four Noble Truths, washin' away the pain.
The Twelve Links of Dependent Origination, how it all takes hold,
From ignorance to old age and death, a story to unfold.

"All exists by birth's condition, a chain we must unbind,
You should all know such faults and suffering, for all of humankind."
When he laid down this Dharma, six hundred million strong,
Reached the end of all their suffering, where they truly do belong.

They all became arhats, free from every ill,
When he preached for the second time, standing strong and still.
Millions of millions of beings, like the Ganges' flowing sand,
Didn't accept the Dharmas, became arhats in the land.

From then on, those who found the Way, their number couldn't be told,
Calculations of a million kalpas, a story to unfold.
At that time, sixteen princes, left their homes, a solemn vow,
Became young śrāmaṇeras, asking "Teach us now!"

"Expound the Great Vehicle Dharma, with wisdom clear and bright,
We and our whole retinue, will see the Buddha's light.
We wish to be like you, World-Honored One, so pure and grand,
Whose wisdom eye is supreme, across this troubled land."

The Buddha knew their hearts, the practices they'd known,
With immeasurable causes, the seeds that they had sown.
With all kinds of parables, he made the message clear,
Preached the six pāramitās, banishin' all fear.

And the matter of supernatural powers, mysteries revealed,
Differentiated true Dharma, on this sacred field.
The path that Bodhisattvas practice, with strength and gentle hand,
He preached this Lotus Sutra, across the troubled land.

In verses like the Ganges' sands, a never-ending flow,
When that Buddha finished preaching, a quiet room he did go.
Into deep meditation, for eighty-four thousand kalpas, long and still,
While the śrāmaṇeras knew, he hadn't moved his will.

For immeasurable millions, they preached his wisdom high,
Each sat on a Dharma seat, beneath the boundless sky.
Preaching this Great Vehicle sutra, while the Buddha kept his pace,
Expounded and helped in his Dharma conversion, with an easy, gentle grace.

Each and every śrāmaṇera, converted all they found,
From six hundred million million, on holy, sacred ground.
To as many as the Ganges' sands, when that Buddha passed away,
All who heard the Dharma, saw a brand new day.

In all the Buddha lands, born together with their guides,
These sixteen śrāmaṇeras, where the wisdom now resides.
After practicing the Buddha Way, completely, true, and bright,
Are now in the ten directions, shining forth their light.

Each attained true enlightenment, a beacon in the night,
Those who heard the Dharma then, are now bathing in their light.
At the place of each of those Buddhas, where their wisdom freely flows,
Those who dwell as śrāvakas, the Buddha Way now grows.

I was among the sixteen, I once preached to you all,
For this reason, with expedient means, I answered every call.
I guided you to Buddha's wisdom, a path both pure and deep,
It's because of this past connection, the promises I keep.

That I now preach the Lotus Sutra, so listen to my plea,
To cause you to enter the Buddha Way, just follow me.
You must not be surprised, no reason to be afraid,
A journey through the darkness, a life completely made.

It's like a dangerous and evil road, where shadows creep and crawl,
A distant, desolate place, where poisonous beasts enthrall.
Without water or grass, a place that people fear,
But a guide can lead you through, when the path is rough and sheer.

An immeasurable number of millions, on this perilous track,
Wish to pass through this dangerous road, there's no turning back.
The road is vast and far, five hundred yojanas long,
But a strong, intelligent guide, will help you overcome the wrong.

His mind is clear and firm, he helps the multitude in danger's way,
But the multitude is weary, they cry out, "No more today!"
They say to the wise guide, "We're completely exhausted now,
And wish to turn back from here, we're ready to take a bow."

The guide thinks to himself, with a pitiful, sad sigh,
"How can they wish to turn back, and let the great treasures lie?"
He immediately thinks of an expedient means, a plan so wise and bold,
And uses his supernatural power, a story to be told.

He creates a great city, with an outer wall so grand,
Adornin' it with houses, across the barren land.
Around, there are gardens and forests, canals and bathing ponds,
With tall gates and towers, a city that responds.

Filled with men and women, a phantom, sweet and kind,
He comforts the multitude, tells them "Peace of mind!"
"You can enter this city, do whatever you wish to do,"
And when the people enter, their hearts are filled with joy anew.

They feel at peace and at ease, they think they've found their rest,
The guide knows they are rested, put to the ultimate test.
He gathers all the multitude, says, "You should go on now, my friend,
This is just a phantom city, not the journey's end."

"I saw that you were weary, wished to turn back from the start,
So with the power of expedient means, I healed your broken heart.
I temporarily created this city, a rest stop on the way,
You must now diligently progress, and we'll reach a brighter day."

"We will go together, to the place where treasures gleam,"
I am also like this, the guide in every dream.
I see all who seek the Way, get lazy, give up hope,
Unable to pass through the road, with its dangerous, slippery slope.

Of life, death, and all afflictions, the burdens that we bear,
So with the power of expedient means, for their rest, I declare:
I preach nirvana, "Your suffering is extinguished, don't you see?
What you had to do is completed, now you can be free."

When they know they've reached nirvana, and all have come to be,
Arhats, pure and shining, for all the world to see,
Then I gather the great assembly, preach the true Dharma's light,
The Buddhas use the power of expedient means, to make the wrong things right.

To differentiate and speak, of the three vehicles so grand,
But there is only the One Buddha Vehicle, across this weary land.
The two were spoken of as a rest stop, a temporary, sweet release,
Now I will tell you the truth, to bring your soul to peace.

What you have attained is not true extinction, a lesson to behold,
To attain the Buddha's All-Knowing Wisdom, a story to be told.
You must give rise to great diligence, let your spirit softly gleam,
When you have realized All-Knowing Wisdom, like a sweet and gentle dream.

The ten powers, and other Dharmas, of the Buddha, pure and bright,
And are complete in the thirty-two marks, that is the true extinction's light.
The guides of all Buddhas, preach nirvana as a stop,
When they know it is a rest stop, they lead them to the top.

Into the Buddha's wisdom, where peace and joy reside,
With open hearts and spirits, and nothing left to hide.

The Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma, Volume Four
Translated by Tripitaka Master Kumarajiva of the Kucha Kingdom in the Later Qin Dynasty, by imperial decree.


Chapter 8: Bestowal of Prophecies upon Five Hundred Disciples

At that time, Pūrṇa-Maitrāyaṇīputra, having heard from the Buddha this wisdom of expedient means, this preaching of the Dharma according to what is appropriate, and having heard the prophecies for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi for the great disciples, and having heard of the past life karmic connections, and having heard of the great supernatural powers of the Buddhas, felt an unprecedented joy and purity in his heart.
He immediately rose from his seat, went before the Buddha, bowed his head at the Buddha's feet, and then stood to one side, looking up at the revered face of the Buddha without taking his eyes off him. He thought: "The World-Honored One is so wonderful and rare! He follows the various natures of the world and preaches the Dharma with the wisdom of expedient means, pulling sentient beings out of their attachments everywhere. We cannot express the merits of the Buddha in words. Only the World-Honored One can know our deepest hearts and our original vows."
At that time, the Buddha said to all the monks: "Do you all see this Pūrṇa-Maitrāyaṇīputra? I always praise him as the foremost among those who preach the Dharma. I also constantly praise his various merits. He is diligent in protecting and assisting in the preaching of my Dharma. He can guide and benefit the four groups of the assembly, fully explaining the true Dharma of the Buddha and bringing great benefit to those who practice the same pure conduct. Other than the Tathagata himself, there is no one who can exhaust his eloquence and debate."
"You should not think that Pūrṇa is only able to protect and assist in the preaching of my Dharma. In the past, under ninety million Buddhas, he also protected and assisted in the preaching of the true Dharma of the Buddhas. Among those who preached the Dharma, he was also the foremost. Moreover, he has a clear and unhindered understanding of the Dharma of emptiness preached by the Buddhas, and he has attained the four unhindered wisdoms. He can always preach the Dharma purely with careful consideration, without any doubt, and is complete in the supernatural powers of a Bodhisattva. Throughout his life, he always cultivated pure conduct. The people of those Buddha worlds all truly believed him to be a śrāvaka. But Pūrṇa, with these expedient means, brought benefit to immeasurable hundreds of thousands of sentient beings, and he also converted immeasurable asaṃkhyeya people, causing them to establish the resolve for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. For the sake of purifying a Buddha land, he constantly does the work of a Buddha and converts sentient beings."
"Monks, Pūrṇa was also the foremost among those who preached the Dharma under the Seven Buddhas of the past, and he is the foremost among those who preach the Dharma under me today. Among the Buddhas who will appear in the Bhadrakalpa (the present auspicious kalpa), he will also be the foremost among those who preach the Dharma. He will also protect and assist in the preaching of the Dharma of immeasurable and boundless Buddhas in the future, converting and benefiting immeasurable sentient beings and causing them to establish the resolve for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. For the sake of purifying a Buddha land, he will always diligently progress in converting sentient beings and will gradually be complete in the Bodhisattva Way. After immeasurable asaṃkhyeya kalpas, he will, in this very land, attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, with the title Dharma-Light Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One."
That Buddha will have a Buddha land as vast as the three-thousand-great-thousand-fold world, and the ground will be made of the seven treasures, level as a palm, without any mountains, hills, streams, valleys, or ditches. Jeweled towers and pavilions will fill it. The palaces of the gods will be close to the sky, and humans and gods will be able to see one another. There will be no evil destinies and no women. All sentient beings will be born by transformation and will have no sexual desire. They will have great supernatural powers, and light will emanate from their bodies. They will be able to fly freely, their resolve will be firm, they will be diligent in their wisdom, and all of them will have golden bodies adorned with the thirty-two marks. The sentient beings in that land will always have two kinds of food: one, the food of Dharma joy, and two, the food of meditation joy. There will be an immeasurable number of asaṃkhyeya tens of millions of nayuta Bodhisattva assemblies, who have attained great supernatural powers and the four unhindered wisdoms, and who are skilled at converting all kinds of sentient beings. The śrāvaka assemblies will be so numerous they cannot be known by calculation. They will all be complete in the six supernatural powers, the three wisdoms, and the eight liberations. That Buddha land will be adorned with these immeasurable merits. The kalpa will be named Jewel-Light, and the land will be named Good-Purification. The Buddha's life span will be immeasurable asaṃkhyeya kalpas. The Dharma will remain for a very long time. After the Buddha's passing, seven-jeweled stupas will be erected, filling his land.
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
Monks, lend an ear, let the truth unfold,
The Buddha's son, a story to be told.
He walks the path, with means so sly and deep,
His every move, a secret he does keep.
He sees the souls, who crave the small delight,
And fear the wisdom, grand and shining bright.
So Bodhisattvas, with a humble guise,
Like śrāvakas and pratyekabuddhas rise.
With countless tricks, they turn the hearts of man,
Converting all, according to their plan.
They say they're śrāvakas, far from the Buddha's call,
But countless beings they save, and stand up tall.
Though small their wants, and lazy they may seem,
They'll rise to Buddhas, fulfilling every dream.
Inside, the practice of a Bodhisattva's kept,
Outside, a śrāvaka, while the world has slept.
They crave so little, from this life they shrink,
Yet purifying lands, on the very brink.
They show the poisons, three in number strong,
And even wrong views, where they don't belong.
My own disciples, they are just the same,
Using sly means, to spread the saving flame.
If I told all, their changes, every one,
Doubt would fill hearts, before the day was done.
Now Pūrṇa here, a man of steadfast ways,
Served countless Buddhas, through a thousand days.
He helped them preach, their Dharma clear and true,
For wisdom's sake, beneath the sky so blue.
He stood above, the disciples of his time,
Heard much and learned, with wisdom so sublime.
He preached without fear, made the assembly cheer,
Never grew weary, banishing all fear.
Great powers he gained, with wisdom, sharp and keen,
Knowing all minds, the dull, the bright, unseen.
He preached the Dharma, pure and free from stain,
Teaching millions, easing all their pain.
Leading to the Vehicle, grand and wide,
His own Buddha land, where good things will abide.
In future times, more Buddhas he will meet,
Offering gifts, from head down to his feet.
He'll guard the Dharma, true and ever bold,
And purify his land, a story to unfold.
With skillful means, he'll preach without a doubt,
Saving countless souls, putting fear to rout.
To All-Knowing Wisdom, he'll lead them on their way,
Serving Tathagatas, until the break of day.
Protecting Dharma's treasures, old and new,
Then Buddhahood he'll gain, with a light so true.
Dharma-Light his name, when his time is near,
Good-Purification, his land, banishing all fear.
Seven treasures gleaming, a sight to behold,
Jewel-Light the kalpa, a story to be told.
Bodhisattvas gather, a multitude so grand,
With mighty powers, filling all the land.
Śrāvakas countless, with wisdom and release,
His monastic gathering, finding inner peace.
No sexual longing, in that land so bright,
Born pure and transformed, in the Dharma's light.
Their bodies adorned, with marks of grace and might,
Dharma joy their food, day and through the night.
No other craving, for what the world can bring,
No women there, no evil, everything's a spring. 
Pūrṇa-Maitrāyaṇīputra, his merits all complete, 
This pure land he'll gain, with sages at his feet.
These countless matters, I've spoken but a few,
The depth and glory, shining ever new.
At that time, the twelve hundred Arhats, whose minds were free, thought: "We are so joyful and have gained what we have never had. If the World-Honored One were to give each of us a prophecy like he did the other great disciples, would that not also be wonderful?"
The Buddha knew the thoughts in their hearts and said to Mahākāśyapa: "I will now give prophecies to these twelve hundred arhats, one by one, in your presence, for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. In this assembly, my great disciple, the monk Ajñāta-Kauṇḍinya, will make offerings to six hundred and twenty thousand million Buddhas and will then attain Buddhahood, with the title Universal-Light Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. The five hundred arhats—Uruvilva-Kāśyapa, Gayā-Kāśyapa, Nadī-Kāśyapa, Kāludāyin, Udayin, Aniruddha, Revata, Kapphiṇa, Bakkula, Cunda, Svāgata, and others—will all attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, and their titles will all be the same, Universal-Light.”
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
Now listen here, to a tale I'll impart,
Of Ajñāta-Kauṇḍinya, with a pure, searching heart.
He gonna see Buddhas, a sight to behold,
Through countless long kalpas, a story untold.
Yeah, he'll find true enlightenment, shining so bright,
Gonna beam out great light, day and through the long night.
Got them supernatural powers, complete and so grand,
His fame gonna echo, throughout every land.

Hear his name in the ten directions, a sweet, soulful sound,
Revered by all beings, wherever they're found.
He'll preach the supreme Way, with a wisdom so deep,
Universal-Light his title, secrets to keep.

His land gonna be pure, like a clear, morning dew,
Bodhisattvas so valiant, fierce and so true.
They'll climb them high towers, them pavilions so grand,
Travel through the ten directions, hand in glorious hand.

To offer up offerings, to the Buddhas above,
With hearts full of joy, and a whole lot of love.
Then back to their homeland, in a blink of an eye,
Such great supernatural power, reaching for the sky.

The Buddha's life span, sixty thousand kalpas strong,
The True Dharma double that, where it truly belongs.
The Dharma-Image double again, a sight to perceive,
When Dharma is gone, gods and humans gonna grieve.

Now the five hundred monks, one after the other,
Gonna reach Buddhahood, like a dear, loving brother.
Their title the same, Universal-Light they will be,
Prophecies given, for all eyes to see.

After my passing, someone's gonna rise,
Become a great Buddha, with wisdom in his eyes.
The world he converts, gonna look just like mine,
Adornments and purity, a truly divine design.

All them supernatural powers, shining so free,
Bodhisattva and śrāvaka, for all souls to see.
The True Dharma, Dharma-Image, a spiritual art,
The life span and kalpas, played right from the start.

Just like I said, it's gonna be just so,
Kāśyapa, you hear me, gotta let you know.
The five hundred arhats, free in their mind,
And them śrāvaka assemblies, of the same blessed kind.

For those not here with us, lost in the blue,
You gotta preach this message, carry it through.
At that time, the five hundred arhats, having received a prophecy in the presence of the Buddha, were filled with joy and delight. They immediately rose from their seats, went before the Buddha, and bowed their heads at his feet, repenting and reproaching themselves.
“World-Honored One, we always thought: ‘We have already attained ultimate extinction.’ But now we know we were like ignorant people. Why? We should have attained the Buddha's wisdom, but we were content with our little wisdom.”
The Parable of the Pearl in the Robe
“World-Honored One, it is like a person who goes to a friend's house and, having become drunk, falls asleep. At that time, the friend had an official matter to attend to and was about to leave. He took a priceless jewel and sewed it inside the person's robe and then went away. The person, being drunk and asleep, was completely unaware of it. When he woke up, he traveled to another country. For the sake of clothing and food, he diligently struggled to make a living. It was extremely difficult, and if he gained a little, he would be content with that.
Later, the friend met him by chance and said: ‘Hey, my good man! Why do you struggle for clothing and food like this? I wanted you to be happy and at ease and enjoy the five desires. On a certain day of a certain month in a certain year, I sewed a priceless jewel inside your robe, and it is still there now. But you do not know it, and you labor with great difficulty and worry to sustain your life. This is so foolish! You can now use this jewel to trade for whatever you need and can always have what you wish for, without any lack.’”
The Application of the Parable
“The Buddha is also like this. When you were a Bodhisattva, you taught and converted us, causing us to give rise to the mind for All-Knowing Wisdom. But we soon became neglectful and forgot it, and we were unaware of it. When we attained the arhat Way, we thought we had attained extinction. Like that man struggling to live, we gained a little and were content with it. But our vow for All-Knowing Wisdom was still there and was not lost.
Today, the World-Honored One has awakened us and said: ‘Monks, what you have attained is not ultimate extinction. I have long ago caused you to plant the good roots of a Buddha, and with expedient means, I showed you the form of nirvana, but you thought that you had truly attained extinction.’
World-Honored One, we now know that we are truly Bodhisattvas who will receive the prophecy for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. Because of this, we are filled with great joy and have gained what we never had before.”
At that time, Ajñāta-Kauṇḍinya and others, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
Peace in our hearts, nowhere else to be found.
Joy overflowing, a feeling so new,
Homage to Buddha, His wisdom so true.

Lord of the World, we stand here today,
Repent all our faults, then we kneel and we pray.
Buddha's rich treasures, a small bit we knew,
Thought it was enough, like a fool through and through.

Like a poor soul at a rich friend's door,
Feasting on goodies, then wanting no more.
Friend sews a jewel, deep in his robe's fold,
Gives it in silence, a story untold.

He sleeps through it all, then he wakes and he roams,
Seeks food and clothing, far from his own homes.
Life's a hard road, just a struggle to see,
Content with a pittance, as poor as can be.

Unaware of the jewel, hidden away,
In his own garment, come what may.
Friend finds him later, heart heavy with pain,
Shows him the jewel, again and again.

Poor man sees it, his spirit takes flight,
Joy fills his being, with all of its might.
With these possessions, all five desires he'll find,
Freedom to revel, leaving troubles behind.

We are the same, in this long, lonely night,
World-Honored One taught us, with love and with light.
Planted the vow, though we didn't quite know,
Ignorant, foolish, we watched our lives flow.

Small piece of nirvana, we thought it was grand,
Content with our lot, across this wide land.
Now Buddha awakens, says "This ain't the end,
True wisdom you'll find, on that, you depend."

Now we hear the prophecies, clear as a bell,
Glorious futures, a story to tell.
Bodies and minds, filled with joy, it is true,
Buddha's own wisdom, shining through and through.


Chapter 9: Bestowal of Prophecies upon Arhats and Pratyekabuddhas

At that time, Ānanda and Rāhula thought to themselves: "If we were to receive a prophecy, would that not also be wonderful?"
They immediately rose from their seats, went before the Buddha, bowed their heads at his feet, and together said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, we too should have a share in this. Only in the Tathagata do we find our refuge. Moreover, we are known by all the worlds of gods, humans, and asuras. Ānanda has always been your attendant and has protected the Dharma treasury. Rāhula is your son. If the Buddha gives us a prophecy for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, our wishes will be fulfilled, and the hopes of the assembly will also be met."
At that time, the two thousand disciples who were still "learners" or were "non-learners" all rose from their seats, bared their right shoulders, went before the Buddha, joined their palms with a single mind, and looked up at the World-Honored One. Just like Ānanda and Rāhula, they stood to one side, holding the same wish.
Prophecy for Ānanda
At that time, the Buddha said to Ānanda: "In a future life, you will attain Buddhahood. Your title will be King of All-Penetrating-Wisdom of Mountains and Oceans Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One.
You will serve sixty-two hundred million Buddhas and protect the Dharma treasury, and only then will you attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. You will convert twenty thousand million nayuta Bodhisattvas, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, and cause them to attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. Your land will be named Banner of Constant-Victory, and its ground will be pure and made of lapis lazuli. The kalpa will be named Sound-Filling-Everything. The life span of that Buddha will be immeasurable millions of millions of asaṃkhyeya kalpas. If a person were to try to calculate it over millions of millions of immeasurable asaṃkhyeya kalpas, they would not be able to know its length. The True Dharma will remain in the world for a period double his life span, and the Dharma-Image will last for double the True Dharma. Ānanda, this King of All-Penetrating-Wisdom of Mountains and Oceans Buddha will be universally praised by the immeasurable millions of millions of Tathagatas, as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, in the ten directions, who will extol his merits."
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
Listen close now, hear what I say,
Among the monks, I declare this day:
Ānanda, keeper of the righteous way, 
He'll serve the Buddhas, come what may.
Then true enlightenment, he will find,
Leave all his earthly troubles behind.
King of All-Penetrating-Wisdom, they'll call his name,
Of Mountains and Oceans, fueling his sacred flame.
His land will be pure, a sight to behold,
Banner of Constant-Victory, a story untold.
Bodhisattvas he'll convert, like sands on the shore,
Their numbers are countless, seeking something more.
That Buddha's got majesty, a virtue so deep,
His fame fills ten directions, while the whole world does sleep.
His life span's immeasurable, a truth to embrace,
Compassion for all beings, in time and in space.
The True Dharma will double his life, so they say,
And the Dharma-Image doubles again, come what may.
Countless beings, like Ganges sands, so vast and wide,
In that Buddha's Dharma, the Buddha Way, they'll abide.
At that time, eight thousand newly resolved Bodhisattvas in the assembly all thought: "We have not even heard of great Bodhisattvas receiving such prophecies. What is the reason that these śrāvakas are receiving such a definitive promise?"
At that time, the World-Honored One, knowing the thoughts in the hearts of the Bodhisattvas, said to them: "Noble men, Ānanda and I gave rise to the mind for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi at the same time, under the Buddha King of Emptiness. Ānanda always delighted in hearing much, and I always cultivated diligent progress. For this reason, I have already attained Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, while Ānanda protects my Dharma and will also protect the Dharma treasury of all future Buddhas, converting and bringing to completion the assemblies of Bodhisattvas. His original vow was like this, and so he receives this prophecy."
When Ānanda heard the Buddha give him a prophecy in his presence and describe the adornments of his future land, all his wishes were fulfilled. His heart was filled with great joy and he felt an unprecedented happiness. He immediately recalled the Dharma treasuries of immeasurable millions of Buddhas from the past, and he understood them all without hindrance, just as he had heard the present Dharma, and he also remembered his original vow. At that time, Ānanda spoke in verse:
The World-Honored One, so rarely seen,
Got me lookin' back at where I've been.
Buddhas' teachings, a countless, flowing tide,
Like I'm hearing 'em for the first time, deep inside.

Now my doubts have all just faded away,
Settled on the Buddha's path, come what may.
I've served as an attendant, with a helpful hand,
Protecting those Dharmas, across the land.
Prophecy for Rāhula and the 2,000 Disciples
At that time, the Buddha said to Rāhula: "In a future life, you will attain Buddhahood. Your title will be Treading-on-Seven-Jeweled-Flowers Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. You will make offerings to a number of Buddhas as numerous as the dust motes in ten worlds. You will always be the eldest son of all the Buddhas, just as you are now. The land of this Treading-on-Seven-Jeweled-Flowers Buddha, his life span, the kalpa, the disciples he converts, the True Dharma, and the Dharma-Image will be no different from that of King of All-Penetrating-Wisdom of Mountains and Oceans Tathagata, and you will also be the eldest son of this Buddha. After this, you will attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi."
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
When I was a young prince, a long time ago,
Rāhula, my eldest, watched my spirit grow.
Now I've found the Buddha Way, a truth deep and old,
And he's my Dharma son, a story to be told.

In lifetimes yet to come, a vision I can see,
He'll meet countless Buddhas, for all eternity.
He'll be their eldest son, with a heart pure and true,
Seeking the Buddha Way, in all that he will do.

Rāhula's secret walk, a path only I discern,
He plays my eldest son, for all the world to learn.
His merits, vast and grand, beyond all numbers known,
Settled in the Dharma, on wisdom's sacred throne.
At that time, the World-Honored One saw the two thousand disciples, both learners and non-learners, whose intentions were gentle, still, and pure, and who were looking at the Buddha with a single mind. The Buddha said to Ānanda: "Do you see these two thousand learners and non-learners?"
"Yes, I do," he replied.
"Ānanda, these people will make offerings to a number of Tathagatas as numerous as the dust motes in fifty worlds. They will show them respect and reverence and protect the Dharma treasury. In their final life, they will all simultaneously attain Buddhahood in the lands of the ten directions. Their title will all be the same: Jewel-Form Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. Their life span will be one kalpa. The adornments of their lands, their śrāvakas and Bodhisattvas, and their True Dharma and Dharma-Image will all be the same."
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
These two thousand śrāvakas, standin' right before my eyes,
Gonna get their prophecies, reachin' for the skies.
Buddhas they will serve, countless as the dust, you see,
Guardin' Dharma's treasure, for all eternity.

In their lands so far, in directions ten they'll roam,
Same old title they will share, feelin' right at home.
Gonna sit in enlightenment, at the self-same time,
Reachin' for that wisdom, in a holy, sacred climb.

Jewel-Form their name will be, shinin' ever bright,
Lands and all their people, bathed in holy light.
True Dharma, Dharma-Image, all the same, no doubt,
Every single thing in common, shoutin' it all about.

With their wondrous powers, savin' every soul,
Hear their fame echo, makin' spirits whole.
Slowly into nirvana, they'll softly fade away,
Leavin' peace and wisdom, to light up every day.
