Like crystal lapis lazuli, bright and clean,
The finest sight the people ever seen.

It's like a mirror, polished bright and true,
Reflecting all the forms that pass right through.
The Bodhisattva's body, pure and free,
Sees all the world, but only he can see.

The living things in all the three-fold lands,
The gods and demons held within his hands.
The poor ghosts walkin', and the beasts that creep,
Their shapes reflected, while the world's asleep.

The halls of heaven, up so high they go,
The mountains standing, where the wild winds blow.
The deep blue ocean, and the waters wide,
All things within that body do abide.

The Buddhas preachin', and the followers near,
They're all reflected, banishin' the fear.
Though he ain't got that perfect nature yet,
This common body holds the whole world's debt.

The Merits of the Mind
"Furthermore, Constant Diligence, if a noble man or noble woman, after the Tathagata's passing, upholds this sutra, or reads, recites, explains, or copies it, they will attain twelve hundred merits for the mind. With this pure mind faculty, upon hearing even one verse or one line, they will penetrate the immeasurable and boundless meanings. Having understood this meaning, they can then expound on a single line or a single verse for a month, for four months, or even for a year. What he preaches, according to its meaning, will not be at odds with the true nature of all phenomena.
"If he preaches on worldly scriptures, on the words of governance, or on the work of sustaining life, it will all be in accordance with the true Dharma. The thoughts, actions, and verbal games of all sentient beings in the six destinies of the three-thousand-great-thousand-fold world, he will know them all. Although he has not yet attained the wisdom of unconditioned reality, his mind faculty is already this pure. Whatever this person thinks, contemplates, or speaks, it is all the Buddha Dharma, and it is all true. It is also what has been preached in the sutras of the Buddhas of the past."
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
That mind so pure and clean,
Sharp as a tack, ain't got no mean.
With that sweet mind a-workin' free,
Knows the high and the low, for all to see.

Hears just one verse, hear me now,
Unlocks deep meanings, don't know how.
Preachin' the Dharma, in the right way,
A month, four months, or a whole year, day by day.

All the folks in this wide world 'round,
Inside and outside, on holy ground.
Gods, dragons, and the human race,
Yakshas and the spirits, keepin' up the pace.

All their mixed-up thoughts, deep and low,
In the six pathways where the souls must go.
'Cause he's holdin' fast to the Lotus sound,
He knows 'em all when he looks around.

Countless Buddhas, ten directions bright,
Shinin' with them hundred marks of light.
Preachin' the Dharma for the souls in need,
He hears it all, plants the holy seed.

Thinks on them meanings, wide and vast,
His preachin' goes on, it's built to last.
Don't forget a thing, from start to end,
'Cause he's got that Lotus Sutra, his truest friend.

Knows the true nature of all that is,
Understands the order, that's his biz.
Knows all the names and the words they speak,
Preaches it straight, ain't no need to sneak.

Whatever comes from his lips, you see,
It's the Buddhas' Dharma from history.
Expounds this truth, without no fright,
Standin' in the crowd, shinin' oh so bright.

Mind of the one holdin' this book in hand,
Pure as a bell, right across the land.
Ain't got to Nirvana, not yet today,
But he got these signs, showin' him the way.

This soul who keeps this Sutra near,
Walks on a rare ground, have no fear.
All the livin' creatures, near and far,
They love him, yeah, he's a lucky star.

Uses a thousand kinds of gentle tongue,
Skillful words, a sweet song he's sung.
To break it all down and preach it true,
'Cause he's holdin' that Lotus, me and you.

Chapter 20: The Bodhisattva Never Disparaging

At that time, the Buddha said to Bodhisattva-Mahāsattva Great-Power: "You should now know that if a monk, nun, layman, or laywoman who upholds the Lotus Sutra is slandered and abused with evil words, the great karmic retribution they receive is as I have said before. The merit they gain is the purification of the eyes, ears, nose, tongue, body, and mind, as I have also said before.
Great-Power, in the distant past, an immeasurable, boundless, and inconceivable asaṃkhyeya kalpas ago, there was a Buddha named King of Awesome Sound Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. The kalpa was named Leaving-Decay, and the land was named Great-Completion. This King of Awesome Sound Buddha, in that world, preached the Dharma for gods, humans, and asuras. For those who sought the śrāvaka path, he preached the Dharma of the Four Noble Truths to save them from birth, old age, sickness, and death and lead them to ultimate nirvana. For those who sought the pratyekabuddha path, he preached the Dharma of the Twelve Links of Dependent Origination. For the Bodhisattvas, he preached the Dharma of the six pāramitās for the sake of Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, ultimately leading them to the wisdom of the Buddha.
Great-Power, this King of Awesome Sound Buddha's life span was four hundred thousand million nayuta kalpas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges. The number of kalpas that his True Dharma remained in the world was as many as the dust motes of a single Jambudvīpa. The number of kalpas that his Dharma-Image remained in the world was as many as the dust motes of four four-continents. After that Buddha brought great benefit to sentient beings, he passed away. After the True Dharma and Dharma-Image had been completely extinguished, in that land, another Buddha appeared, also named King of Awesome Sound Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. In this way, there were twenty hundred million Buddhas, all with the same title."
The Bodhisattva Never Disparaging
"After the first King of Awesome Sound Tathagata had passed away and his True Dharma had been extinguished, in the period of the Dharma-Image, the arrogant monks were a great force. At that time, there was a Bodhisattva monk named Never Disparaging. Great-Power, for what reason was he named Never Disparaging? This monk, whenever he saw a person—whether they were a monk, nun, layman, or laywoman—he would bow in reverence to them and praise them, saying: 'I deeply revere all of you, and I do not dare to hold you in contempt. Why? Because you will all practice the Bodhisattva Way and will attain Buddhahood.'
"This monk did not exclusively read or recite the scriptures. He only bowed and paid reverence. Even when he saw the four groups of the assembly from a distance, he would still go and bow to them and praise them, saying: 'I do not dare to hold you in contempt. You will all attain Buddhahood.' Among the four groups of the assembly, those who gave rise to a mind of anger and impurity and abused him with evil words said: 'Where has this ignorant monk come from? He claims not to hold us in contempt, but he gives us a prophecy that we will attain Buddhahood. We do not need such a false prophecy.'
"In this way, after many years, he was constantly abused, but he did not give rise to a mind of anger. He always said: 'You will attain Buddhahood.' When he spoke these words, people would sometimes hit him with sticks, wood, tiles, or stones. He would run away and stand at a distance, and would still say in a loud voice: 'I do not dare to hold you in contempt. You will all attain Buddhahood.' Because he always spoke these words, the arrogant monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen gave him the name Never Disparaging."
The Karmic Connection
"When this monk was about to pass away, he heard from the empty sky the Lotus Sutra that King of Awesome Sound Buddha had previously preached, in twenty hundred million verses. He was able to receive and uphold all of it and immediately attained the purification of the six sense faculties—the eyes, ears, nose, tongue, body, and mind, as mentioned above. Having attained this purification of the six sense faculties, he gained a longer life of two hundred million million nayuta years and widely preached the Lotus Sutra to people. At that time, the arrogant four groups who had held him in contempt and given him the name Never Disparaging, saw that he had attained great supernatural power, the power of joyful eloquence, and the power of great stillness. When they heard his preaching, they all believed and submitted, and followed him.
"This Bodhisattva also converted hundreds of thousands of millions of beings, causing them to dwell in Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. After he passed away, he encountered two hundred thousand million Buddhas, all named Sun Moon Lamp Light, and in their Dharma, he preached the Lotus Sutra. Because of this cause, he again encountered two hundred thousand million Buddhas, all named King of Cloud-Sovereign-Lamp. In the Dharma of all these Buddhas, he received and upheld, read, and recited this sutra. Because he preached this scripture for the four groups of the assembly, he attained the constant purity of the eyes, ears, nose, tongue, body, and mind. When he preached the Dharma for the four groups, his heart was fearless."
"Great-Power, this Bodhisattva-Mahāsattva Never Disparaging made offerings to countless Buddhas in this way, with reverence, respect, and praise, and planted roots of goodness. In a later time, he again encountered thousands of millions of Buddhas, and he also preached this scripture in their Dharma. With the completion of his merits, he was able to attain Buddhahood.
"Great-Power, what do you think? Was the Bodhisattva Never Disparaging of that time a different person? He was myself. If I had not, in my past lives, received and upheld, read, and recited this sutra and preached it for others, I could not have so quickly attained Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. It was because I, in the presence of past Buddhas, received, upheld, read, and recited this sutra and preached it for others that I quickly attained Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi.
"Great-Power, the four groups of the assembly at that time—the monks, nuns, laymen, and laywomen—who, with a mind of anger, held me in contempt, for two hundred million kalpas did not encounter a Buddha, did not hear the Dharma, and did not see the monastic community. For a thousand kalpas, they endured great suffering in the Avīci hell. After their sins were exhausted, they again encountered Bodhisattva Never Disparaging, who converted them to Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi.
"Great-Power, what do you think? Were the four groups who held that Bodhisattva in contempt at that time different people? They are the five hundred Bodhisattvas such as Bhadrapāla, the five hundred monks such as Lion-Moon, and the five hundred laymen such as Nisīśvara in this assembly now, who have all attained the state of non-retrogression from Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. Great-Power, you should know that this Lotus Sutra brings great benefit to the Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas and can cause them to attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. For this reason, all Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas, after the Tathagata’s passing, should constantly receive, uphold, read, recite, explain, and copy this sutra."
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
Long ago there was a Buddha, yes, a man of mighty fame,
King of Awesome Sound, they called him, yeah, that was his holy name.
His spiritual wisdom was boundless, his light shined through the air,
He guided all the beings, Lord, he showed them how to care.

Gods and humans, dragons, spirits, they all came to pray,
Made their little offerings before he passed away.
After that Buddha left us, when the Dharma was on the wane,
Came a Bodhisattva walkin', through the dusty, weary rain.

Never Disparaging, they named him, a good man on the road,
The four groups of the assembly, they carried a heavy load,
Stuck fast to their own teachings, wouldn't open up their mind,
But this Bodhisattva, he left all his troubles behind.

He walked on over to 'em, didn't hold his head up high,
Said, "I ain't gonna hold you in contempt, not 'til the day I die.
You gonna practice the Way, child, that's what you gonna do,
And you gonna attain Buddhahood, me and you and all your crew."

When those folks heard him talkin', they just laughed and turned to scorn,
They despised and they abused him, from the moment he was born.
But Never Disparaging, he just took it on the chin,
He was able to endure it, Lord, and wash away his sin.

After his bad karma faded, and he was gettin' mighty weak,
He heard this blessed sutra, and the words he had to speak,
His six senses got pure, baby, pure as the driven snow,
'Cause of that supernatural power, his life was slow to go.

He preached that sutra widely, all the folks began to hear,
For all the people standin', to wipe away their fear.
Those assemblies stuck in doctrine, they finally understood,
Got that Bodhisattva's teaching, like every good man should.

They were caused to be complete now, they walked that Buddha Way,
Never Disparaging passed away, saw a brighter, better day.
Met countless, countless Buddhas, 'cause he spread that holy sound,
He attained immeasurable blessings, all over the ground.

He completed all his merits, yeah, he did his very best,
And he quickly found the Buddha Way, and laid his soul to rest.
That Never Disparaging, honey, that man from long ago,
That was me, myself, I tell you, that was me, you oughta know.

The four groups of assembly, with their doctrine held so tight,
They heard me say, "You'll be a Buddha," and they finally saw the light.
Because of that good reason, they found a better place,
They met countless, countless Buddhas, yeah, they ran a good, long race.

The five hundred Bodhisattvas, sittin' right here in this place,
And the four groups of pure laypeople, with grace upon their face,
They the ones now in my presence, listenin' to the Dharma's call,
I, in a life before this one, I lifted them up after they fall.

I told 'em to hear this sutra, yeah, the supreme, holy law,
I showed and taught them everything, let 'em see what they never saw.
Caused them to dwell in nirvana, set their weary spirits free,
From lifetime to lifetime, they upheld the words you hear from me.

It took billions and billions of kalpas, a time you can't conceive,
Before they finally heard it, the truth that they believe,
That Lotus Sutra, baby, it's a mighty, precious thing.
For billions and billions of kalpas, the World-Honored Buddhas sing.

So listen to me, practitioners, after the Buddha's gone,
When you hear this blessed sutra, don't you doubt it 'til the morn.
You gotta be of one mind, child, and preach this sutra wide,
And lifetime after lifetime, the Buddha will be your guide.
You gonna meet the Buddha, honey, yeah, you gonna walk the line,
And you will quickly attain the Buddha Way, and everything will be fine.



Chapter 21: The Transcendent Powers of the Tathagata

At that time, the Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas as numerous as the dust motes of a thousand worlds, who had sprung forth from the earth, all stood in the presence of the Buddha. With a single mind, they joined their palms and, looking up at the Buddha's revered face, said: "World-Honored One, after the Buddha's passing, in the lands where your emanations have dwelt and passed away, we will widely preach this sutra. Why? We ourselves wish to attain this truly pure great Dharma and to receive, uphold, read, recite, explain, copy, and make offerings to it."
The Manifestation of the Buddha's Transcendent Powers
At that time, the World-Honored One, in the presence of Mañjuśrī and the immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of old Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas of the Saha world, and all the monks, nuns, laymen, laywomen, gods, dragons, yakshas, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, and non-humans, manifested his great supernatural powers. He extended his long and broad tongue up to the Brahma heavens. From all his pores, he emitted immeasurable and countless lights of different colors, which universally shone throughout all the worlds of the ten directions.
The Buddhas who were sitting on the lion's seats under the jeweled trees also did the same: they extended their long and broad tongues and emitted immeasurable light. Śākyamuni Buddha and the other Buddhas under the jeweled trees manifested their supernatural powers in this way for a full hundred thousand years, and then they retracted their tongues. At the same time, they coughed and snapped their fingers. The sound of these two actions reached all the worlds of the ten directions, and the earth shook in six ways.
The sentient beings in those worlds—the gods, dragons, yakshas, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, and non-humans—by the Buddha's supernatural power, were all able to see this Saha world. They saw the immeasurable and boundless hundreds of thousands of millions of Buddhas sitting on lion’s seats under the jeweled trees. They also saw Śākyamuni Buddha and Abundant Treasures Tathagata sitting on a lion’s seat inside the jeweled stupa. They also saw the immeasurable and boundless hundreds of thousands of millions of Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas and the four groups of the assembly reverently surrounding Śākyamuni Buddha. Having seen this, they were all filled with great joy and felt an unprecedented happiness.
Immediately, the gods in the air loudly proclaimed: "Beyond these immeasurable, boundless, hundreds of thousands of millions of asaṃkhyeya worlds, there is a land named Saha. In this land, there is a Buddha named Śākyamuni, who is now preaching a Great Vehicle sutra for the Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas, named the Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma, a Dharma for Bodhisattvas protected and remembered by the Buddhas. You should all give rise to a deep heart of joyful following and should also pay homage and make offerings to Śākyamuni Buddha."
The sentient beings of those worlds, having heard the voice from the air, joined their palms and, facing the Saha world, said: "Namo Śākyamuni Buddha! Namo Śākyamuni Buddha!" With all kinds of flowers, incense, garlands, banners, canopies, adornments for the body, and precious, wonderful objects, they all scattered them toward the Saha world from afar. All these scattered objects, coming from the ten directions, were like gathering clouds. They became a jeweled canopy that universally covered all the Buddhas here. At that time, all the worlds of the ten directions were connected without hindrance, like one Buddha land.
The Entrustment of the Sutra
At that time, the Buddha said to Superior Conduct and the great assembly of Bodhisattvas: "The supernatural powers of the Buddhas are immeasurable, boundless, and inconceivable. If I were to use these supernatural powers to speak of the merits of this sutra for the purpose of entrusting it, for an immeasurable, boundless, hundreds of thousands of millions of asaṃkhyeya kalpas, I still could not exhaust them. To put it concisely, all the Dharmas that the Tathagata possesses, all the Tathagata's supernatural powers of independence, all the secret treasures of the Tathagata, and all the extremely profound matters of the Tathagata, are all revealed and expounded in this sutra.
"For this reason, after the Tathagata's passing, you should all, with a single mind, receive and uphold, read, recite, explain, copy, and practice it as it is taught. In any land where there is one who receives and upholds, reads, recites, explains, or copies it, or practices it as it is taught—or wherever a scroll of this sutra is kept, whether in a garden, a forest, under a tree, in a monastery, in a layman's house, in a hall, or in a mountain valley or wilderness—a stupa should be erected there and offerings should be made. Why? You should know that this place is the very place of enlightenment. The Buddhas attain Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi here. The Buddhas turn the Dharma wheel here. And the Buddhas enter parinirvāṇa here."
At that time, the World-Honored One, wishing to repeat this meaning, spoke in verse:
The world's great saviors, the Buddhas all know,
Got mighty powers, watch 'em make 'em flow.
To please all the beings, they got a deep need,
Unrollin' those wonders, plantin' a mighty good seed.

They stretch out their tongue to the Brahma sky so high,
From their bodies light pours, watchin' the darkness fly.
For folks searchin' for the Buddha Way, feelin' the call,
They show this rare vision, standin' up tall.

The sound of the Buddhas, a little coughin' sound,
A snap of their fingers, rings the world all around.
Heard in ten directions, yeah, in every single place,
The earth starts to shakin', six ways with grace.

'Cause of those who, after the Buddha's long gone,
Can hold onto this sutra, yeah, from dusk till the dawn,
All the Buddhas are joyful, makin' their power appear,
Unrollin' their wonders, castin' out all fear.

To pass down this teaching, so true and so deep,
And praise those who keep it, while the whole world does sleep,
For endless long ages, can't be told in a day,
The praise still ain't finished, watchin' it all slip away.

This good person's merit, it stretches far and wide,
Got no end to it, ain't got no place to hide,
Like the open space, in ten directions it flies,
You can't find the bottom, lookin' up at the skies.

One who can hold this sutra, holdin' it tight and true,
Done already seen me, and the things that I do,
Seen Abundant Treasures Buddha, sittin' right there on the throne,
And all my reflections, ain't nobody alone.

They've seen me today, preachin' the Dharma so strong,
Convertin' the Bodhisattvas, right where they belong.
The one who can keep this sutra, deep down in their soul,
Makes me and my shadows, completely feel whole.

And that Abundant Treasures, passed on long ago,
We all rejoice together, watchin' the good things grow.
The Buddhas of the present, and those of the past and the time yet to be,
You see 'em, you serve 'em, bringin' 'em joy for free.

That secret Dharma, that treasure they found so bright,
Attained at the place of learnin', bathin' in pure light,
The one who holds this sutra, won't have to wait so long,
Gonna get that same wisdom, singin' a joyful song.

The one who keeps this sutra, understands what it means,
The names and the words, the world that intervenes,
Gonna talk with no stoppin', joy risin' from the soul,
Like the wind through the heavens, yeah, takin' its toll.

After the Tathagata's gone, movin' on to his rest,
He knows the old sutras, passin' the ultimate test,
Their how and their why, the order they're laid out to be,
And preaches 'em truly, for all the world to see.

Like the sun and the moon, shinin' so bright and so far,
He drives out the darkness, wherever you are.
This person walks easy, down here on the ground,
Can chase away the shadows, from all the folks around.

He teaches the Bodhisattvas, a countless, mighty crew,
And guides 'em to the One Vehicle, makin' their dream come true.
So you wise ones listen, hear what I'm tellin' you today,
Hear 'bout these merits, don't you dare look away.

After I'm gone, when my time here is through,
You ought to take up this sutra, do what you got to do.
This person on the Buddha Way, walkin' in the light,
Gonna have no more questions, everything's gonna be right.




Chapter 22: The Final Entrustment
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha rose from his Dharma seat and, manifesting his great supernatural power, used his right hand to touch the heads of the countless Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas, and he said: "I have, for immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of asaṃkhyeya kalpas, cultivated this Dharma of Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, which is difficult to attain. I now entrust it to all of you. You must all, with a single mind, spread this Dharma and cause it to be widely benefited."
In this way, he touched the heads of the Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas three times and said: "I have, for immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of asaṃkhyeya kalpas, cultivated this Dharma of Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi, which is difficult to attain. I now entrust it to all of you. You must receive, uphold, and widely preach this Dharma, causing all sentient beings to hear and know it. Why? The Tathagata has great compassion, no stinginess, and is without fear. He is able to give sentient beings the Buddha's wisdom, the Tathagata's wisdom, and self-attained wisdom. The Tathagata is the great giver of all sentient beings.
You should also follow the Dharma of the Tathagata and not be stingy. In a future life, if there is a noble man or noble woman who believes in the Tathagata's wisdom, you should expound this Lotus Sutra for them, so they may hear and know it, and so they may attain the Buddha's wisdom. If there are sentient beings who do not believe and accept it, you should teach, guide, and give them joy with the other profound Dharmas of the Tathagata. If you are able to do this, you will have repaid the grace of all the Buddhas."
When the Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas heard the Buddha speak these words, they were all filled with great joy throughout their bodies. They became even more respectful, bowing and lowering their heads. With joined palms facing the Buddha, they all spoke in one voice, saying: "As the World-Honored One has commanded, we will fully obey and practice. Yes, World-Honored One, please do not be concerned." The assemblies of Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas, in this way, spoke in one voice three times: "As the World-Honored One has commanded, we will fully obey and practice. Yes, World-Honored One, please do not be concerned."
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha caused all the emanations of the Buddhas who had come from the ten directions to return to their home lands and said: "All you Buddhas, each of you may return to your lands, and the stupa of Abundant Treasures Buddha may return to what it was." When these words were spoken, the immeasurable emanations of the Buddhas from the ten directions who were sitting on the lion's seats under the jeweled trees, and Abundant Treasures Buddha, and the countless asaṃkhyeya great Bodhisattvas such as Superior Conduct, and the four groups of śrāvakas such as Śāriputra, and all the worlds of gods, humans, and asuras, heard what the Buddha said and were all filled with great joy.


Chapter 23: The Former Lives of the Bodhisattva Medicine King

At that time, Bodhisattva Star-King-Flower said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, how does Bodhisattva Medicine King travel and work in this Saha world? World-Honored One, this Bodhisattva Medicine King has performed hundreds of thousands of millions of nayuta of difficult and painful ascetic practices. Excellent, World-Honored One! We wish you would explain a little about this." The gods, dragons, spirits, yakshas, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, and non-humans, as well as the Bodhisattvas who had come from other lands, and the śrāvaka assembly all heard this and were filled with joy.
The Story of the Bodhisattva's Self-Offering
At that time, the Buddha said to Bodhisattva Star-King-Flower: "In the distant past, an immeasurable number of kalpas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, there was a Buddha named Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One.
"That Buddha had eighty million great Bodhisattva-Mahāsattvas and seventy-two times the sands of the Ganges of great śrāvaka assemblies. The Buddha's life span was forty-two thousand kalpas, and the Bodhisattvas' life spans were the same. That land had no women, hells, hungry ghosts, animals, or asuras, and was free from all calamities. The ground was as flat as a palm and made of crystal, adorned with jeweled trees. Jeweled canopies hung above, and jeweled flower banners hung down. Jeweled bottles and incense burners were found everywhere in the land. There were jeweled platforms, one under each tree, and the distance between the tree and the platform was the flight of one arrow. Under these jeweled trees, Bodhisattvas and śrāvakas were sitting. On each of the jeweled platforms, there were ten million heavenly beings who played heavenly music and sang praises to the Buddha as an offering.
"At that time, that Buddha preached the Lotus Sutra for the Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See, and for the other Bodhisattvas and the śrāvaka assemblies. This Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See delighted in cultivating difficult ascetic practices. In the Dharma of the Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue Buddha, he diligently practiced walking meditation. He sought the Buddha with a single mind for twelve thousand years and attained the Samadhi of Manifesting All Forms.
"Having attained this samadhi, his heart was filled with great joy, and he thought: 'My attainment of the Samadhi of Manifesting All Forms is entirely due to the power of hearing the Lotus Sutra. I should now make an offering to the Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue Buddha and the Lotus Sutra.' He then entered this samadhi, and from the sky, rained down maṇḍārava and mahāmaṇḍārava flowers, and fine powder of a firm, black sandalwood, which filled the sky and fell like a cloud. He also rained down the incense of sandalwood from this side of the ocean. The value of six grains of this incense was the equivalent of the entire Saha world. He used this to make an offering to the Buddha.
"Having made this offering, he arose from the samadhi and thought to himself: 'Although I have made offerings to the Buddha with my supernatural power, it is not as good as making an offering with my own body.' He then ingested all kinds of incense—sandalwood, frankincense, aloe, pine resin, agarwood, and gum incense—and drank the fragrant oil of campaka flowers. After twelve hundred years, he anointed his body with the fragrant oil. In the presence of the Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue Buddha, he wrapped his body in a heavenly jeweled robe, poured fragrant oils over himself, and with the power of his spiritual vow, set his body on fire. His light shone universally throughout eighty million worlds as numerous as the sands of the Ganges.
"The Buddhas in those worlds simultaneously praised him, saying: 'Excellent! Excellent! Noble man, this is true diligence! This is called a true Dharma offering to the Tathagata. Offerings of flowers, incense, garlands, burning incense, powdered incense, paste incense, heavenly silks, banners, canopies, and the sandalwood incense from this side of the ocean, or other kinds of offerings, cannot compare to this. Even the giving of one's country, city, wife, and children cannot compare to this. Noble man, this is called the first of all acts of giving. Among all acts of giving, it is the most revered and supreme, because it is a Dharma offering to all the Tathagatas.'
"Having spoken these words, they all fell silent. His body burned for twelve hundred years. After that, his body was completely consumed. After Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See had made such a Dharma offering, he passed away and was reborn in the land of the Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue Buddha, in the house of King Pure-Virtue, sitting in the lotus posture. He was born instantly by transformation. He immediately spoke in verse to his father, the king, saying:
Now listen here, King, it's the truth I'll tell,
When I walked that path, I walked it well.
Got that Samadhi, saw all forms so clear,
Chased after wisdom, banished all my fear.

Worked real hard, put my body on the line,
Gave it to the World-Honored One, a sacred sign.
Searching for that wisdom, the highest kind,
Left my old self, didn't look behind.
"Having spoken this verse, he said to his father: 'The Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue Buddha is still in the world. I previously made an offering to the Buddha and attained the total recall of all sentient beings' languages. I also heard this Lotus Sutra in verses of eight hundred million million nayutas as numerous as jeṅkara, bimvara, and akṣobhya. Great King, I will now go back and make offerings to this Buddha.' Having said this, he immediately sat on a seven-jeweled platform, rose into the air as high as seven tāla trees, went to the Buddha's place, bowed his head at the Buddha's feet, joined his ten fingers, and praised the Buddha in verse:
Your face, oh so wondrous, it shines on through,
Your light, it brightens everything anew.
I just laid my offering down for you,
And now I'm back, Lord, close to you.
"At that time, Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See, having spoken this verse, said to the Buddha: 'World-Honored One, the World-Honored One is still in the world.' At that time, the Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue Buddha said to Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See: 'Noble man, my time for nirvāṇa has arrived. The time for extinction has come. You should prepare a seat for me. I will pass into parinirvāṇa tonight.'
"He also commanded Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See: 'Noble man, I entrust my Buddha Dharma to you and all the Bodhisattvas and great disciples, as well as the Dharma of Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. I also give you the three-thousand-great-thousand-fold world of seven treasures, all the jeweled trees, the jeweled platforms, and the gods who serve me. After my passing, I also entrust all my relics to you. You must cause them to be spread and widely make offerings to them. You should erect thousands of stupas.' In this way, the Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue Buddha, having commanded Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See, passed into nirvāṇa in the latter part of the night.
"At that time, Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See, seeing that the Buddha had passed away, felt grief, sorrow, and longing for the Buddha. He immediately gathered sandalwood from this side of the ocean to make a pyre, made offerings to the Buddha’s body, and burned it. After the fire was extinguished, he collected the relics, made eighty-four thousand jeweled bottles, and erected eighty-four thousand stupas, as tall as the three worlds, adorned with jeweled shafts, with banners, canopies, and various jeweled bells hanging from them.
"At that time, Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See again thought to himself: 'Although I have made these offerings, my heart is still not satisfied. I will now make another offering to the relics.' He then said to the Bodhisattvas, the great disciples, and the gods, dragons, yakshas, and all the great assembly: 'You should all remember with a single mind that I am now making an offering to the relics of the Sun-Moon-Pure-Bright-Virtue Buddha.' Having said this, he immediately, in front of the eighty-four thousand stupas, set his hundred-blessing-adorned arms on fire for seventy-two thousand years to make an offering. He caused countless beings seeking the śrāvaka path, and immeasurable asaṃkhyeya people, to give rise to the mind for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi. He enabled them all to dwell in the Samadhi of Manifesting All Forms."
"At that time, all the Bodhisattvas, gods, humans, and asuras, seeing that his arms were gone, were filled with worry, sorrow, and pity and said: 'This Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See, our teacher who converted us, has now burned his arms and his body is no longer complete.'
"At that time, Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See, in the midst of the great assembly, made this vow: 'I have given up my two arms, and I will surely attain the Buddha's golden body. If this is truly not false, then may my two arms return to what they were before.' When he made this vow, his two arms were naturally restored. This was due to the purity of the Bodhisattva's blessings and wisdom. At that moment, the three-thousand-great-thousand-fold world shook in six ways. Heavenly jeweled flowers rained down, and all the gods and humans felt an unprecedented joy."
The Merit of Upholding the Sutra
"The Buddha said to Bodhisattva Star-King-Flower: 'What do you think? Was that Bodhisattva All-Sentient-Beings-Rejoiced-to-See a different person? He is Bodhisattva Medicine King today. The giving of his body was in this way, in immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of nayuta of times. Star-King-Flower, if a person who has given rise to the mind for Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi can burn their fingers, or even one finger, to make an offering to a Buddha stupa, this is better than giving their country, city, wife, and children, and even the mountains, forests, rivers, and ponds, and all the precious treasures of the three-thousand-great-thousand-fold world as an offering. If a person were to fill the three-thousand-great-thousand-fold world with the seven treasures and offer it to the Buddha, great Bodhisattvas, pratyekabuddhas, and arhats, the merit this person gains is not as great as receiving and upholding this Lotus Sutra, even a single four-line verse. Their blessings are the greatest.'
"Star-King-Flower, it is like the ocean, which is the foremost of all the streams, rivers, and waters. This Lotus Sutra is also like this; among all the sutras preached by the Tathagatas, it is the most profound and supreme. And it is like Mount Sumeru, which is the foremost among all mountains—the earth mountains, black mountains, small and great Iron Ring Mountains, and the ten precious mountains. This Lotus Sutra is also like this; among all the sutras, it is the most supreme. And it is like the moon, which is the foremost among all the stars. This Lotus Sutra is also like this; among the millions of millions of kinds of Dharma scriptures, it is the most illuminating. And it is like the sun, which can dispel all darkness. This sutra is also like this; it can break the darkness of all unwholesome deeds. And it is like a wheel-turning holy king, who is the foremost among all the small kings. This sutra is also like this; it is the king among all sutras. And it is like Śakra, who is the king of the Thirty-three Heavens. This sutra is also like this; it is the king among all sutras. And it is like the great Brahma King, who is the father of all sentient beings. This sutra is also like this; it is the father of all sages, learners, non-learners, and those who give rise to the Bodhisattva mind. And it is like the srotāpanna, sakṛdāgāmin, anāgāmin, arhat, and pratyekabuddha, who are the foremost among all ordinary people. This sutra is also like this; among all the scriptures and Dharmas preached by the Tathagata, the Bodhisattvas, and the śrāvakas, it is the most supreme. It is like the Buddha, who is the King of all Dharmas. This sutra is also like this; it is the King among all sutras."
The Merit for Women and a Final Admonition
"Star-King-Flower, this sutra can save all sentient beings. This sutra can cause all sentient beings to be free from all suffering and affliction. This sutra can bring great benefit to all sentient beings and fulfill their vows. It is like a cool pond that can satisfy all who are thirsty. It is like fire for those who are cold, clothes for those who are naked, a master for a merchant, a mother for a child, a boat for crossing a river, a doctor for the sick, a lamp for the dark, a treasure for the poor, a king for the people, an ocean for a merchant, and a torch that removes darkness. This Lotus Sutra is also like this; it can cause sentient beings to be free from all suffering and sickness, and it can untie all the bonds of life and death. If a person hears this Lotus Sutra, or copies it themselves, or causes others to copy it, the merit they gain is so vast that even with the Buddha's wisdom, one cannot calculate its end. If one copies this sutra scroll and makes offerings of flowers, incense, garlands, burning incense, powdered incense, paste incense, banners, canopies, robes, and all kinds of lamps—ghee lamps, oil lamps, fragrant oil lamps, campaka oil lamps, sumana oil lamps, parūṣaka oil lamps, vārsikā oil lamps, and navamallikā oil lamps—the merit they gain is also immeasurable."
"Star-King-Flower, if a person hears this chapter on the former lives of Bodhisattva Medicine King, they will also attain immeasurable and boundless merits. If a woman hears this chapter on the former lives of Bodhisattva Medicine King and is able to uphold it, this is her last lifetime as a woman; she will not be reborn as a woman again. If, after the Tathagata’s passing, in the latter five hundred years, a woman hears this scripture and practices it as it is taught, upon the end of her life, she will immediately go to the Land of Peace and Joy (Pure Land), and be reborn in a lotus flower on a jeweled seat, surrounded by Amitābha Buddha and the great assembly of Bodhisattvas. She will no longer be tormented by greedy desire, nor by anger and foolishness, nor by arrogance and jealousy. She will attain the supernatural powers of a Bodhisattva and the patience of non-arising.
"Having attained this patience, her eye faculty will be pure. With this pure eye faculty, she will see all the Tathagatas, as numerous as the sands of seven million two hundred thousand million nayuta Ganges Rivers. At that time, these Buddhas will all praise her from a distance, saying: 'Excellent! Excellent, noble woman! You were able, in the Dharma of Śākyamuni Buddha, to receive, uphold, read, recite, contemplate, and preach this sutra for others. The blessings and virtues you have attained are immeasurable and boundless. Fire cannot burn you, and water cannot drown you. Your merits, if a thousand Buddhas were to speak of them together, could not be exhausted. You have now been able to break all the armies of Māra and destroy the armies of life and death. All your other enemies are all crushed and extinguished. Noble woman, hundreds of thousands of Buddhas, with their supernatural powers, are protecting you together. Among all the worlds of gods and humans, there is none who can compare to you, except for a Tathagata. The wisdom and meditation of all the śrāvakas, pratyekabuddhas, and even the Bodhisattvas, are not equal to yours.'
"Star-King-Flower, this Bodhisattva is complete in such merits and the power of wisdom."
"If a person hears this chapter on the former lives of Bodhisattva Medicine King and can rejoice and praise it, in this lifetime, the fragrance of a blue lotus flower will constantly come from their mouth, and the fragrance of sandalwood will constantly come from the pores of their body. The merit they attain is as I have spoken above. For this reason, Star-King-Flower, I entrust this chapter on the former lives of Bodhisattva Medicine King to you. After my passing, in the latter five hundred years, you must widely preach and spread it throughout the world of Jambudvīpa and not allow it to be cut off, so that the evil Māra, Māra's followers, the gods, dragons, yakshas, and Kumbhāṇḍas, etc., will not have an advantage over it."
"Star-King-Flower, you must use the power of your supernatural abilities to protect this sutra. Why? This sutra is a good medicine for the illnesses of the people of Jambudvīpa. If a person is sick and hears this sutra, their sickness will immediately be extinguished, and they will not grow old or die. Star-King-Flower, if you see a person who upholds this sutra, you should fill a blue lotus flower with powdered incense and scatter it upon him. Having scattered it, you should think: 'This person will soon gather grass and sit at the place of enlightenment. He will break all the armies of Māra, blow the Dharma conch, beat the great Dharma drum, and save all sentient beings from the great ocean of birth, old age, sickness, and death.' For this reason, those who seek the Buddha Way, when they see a person who upholds this scripture, should give rise to such a respectful heart."
When this chapter on the former lives of Bodhisattva Medicine King was being preached, eighty-four thousand Bodhisattvas attained the total recall of all sentient beings' languages. Abundant Treasures Tathagata, from within the jeweled stupa, praised Bodhisattva Star-King-Flower, saying: "Excellent! Excellent, Star-King-Flower! You have attained inconceivable merits and were able to ask Śākyamuni Buddha such a matter, which benefits all sentient beings without measure."

The Lotus Sutra of the Wonderful Dharma, Volume Seven
Translated by Tripitaka Master Kumarajiva of the Kucha Kingdom in the Later Qin Dynasty, by imperial decree.
Chapter 24: The Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha emitted light from the tuft of hair on his head, one of the supreme marks of a great being. He also emitted a ray of light from the white hair between his eyebrows, which universally illuminated the worlds of all the Buddhas, as numerous as the sands of a hundred and eighty million million nayuta Ganges Rivers in the east. Beyond that number of worlds, there was a world named Pure-Light Adornment. In that land, there was a Buddha named Pure-Flower-Constellation-King-Wisdom Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. He was surrounded and revered by an immeasurable and boundless assembly of Bodhisattvas, and he was preaching the Dharma. Śākyamuni Buddha's light from his white hair universally shone upon that land.
At that time, in the world of Pure-Light Adornment, there was a Bodhisattva named Wonderful Sound. He had long ago planted roots of all merits and had made offerings to and been close to immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of Buddhas, and he was complete in a profoundly deep wisdom. He had attained the Samadhi of Wonderful Banner Form, the Samadhi of the Lotus Sutra, the Samadhi of Pure Virtue, the Samadhi of the King of Constellation's Play, the Samadhi of Non-Conditionedness, the Samadhi of the Seal of Wisdom, the Samadhi of Understanding All Sentient Beings' Languages, the Samadhi of Accumulating All Merits, the Samadhi of Purity, the Samadhi of Supernatural Play, the Samadhi of the Wisdom Torch, the Samadhi of the Adornment King, the Samadhi of Pure Light, the Samadhi of the Pure Treasury, the Samadhi of Non-Commonness, and the Samadhi of the Sun's Whirlwind. He had attained such great samadhis, numbering hundreds of thousands of millions of times the sands of the Ganges.
When Śākyamuni Buddha's light shone on his body, he immediately said to the Pure-Flower-Constellation-King-Wisdom Buddha: "World-Honored One, I will now go to the Saha world to pay homage to, be close to, and make offerings to Śākyamuni Buddha. I also wish to see the Dharma Prince Bodhisattva Mañjuśrī, Bodhisattva Medicine King, Bodhisattva Valiant-Giver, Bodhisattva Star-King-Flower, Bodhisattva Superior-Conduct, Bodhisattva King of Adornment, and Bodhisattva Medicine-on-High."
At that time, the Pure-Flower-Constellation-King-Wisdom Buddha said to Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound: "Do not be scornful of that land and give rise to a lowly thought. Noble man, that Saha world is high and low and uneven. It is filled with dirt, rocks, mountains, and filth. The Buddha's body is small and low, and the Bodhisattva assemblies are also small in form. Your body is forty-two thousand yojanas tall. My body is six hundred and eighty million yojanas tall. Your body is the most majestic, adorned with hundreds of thousands of millions of blessings, and your light is wonderfully beautiful. For this reason, when you go, do not be scornful of that land, or the Buddha, or the Bodhisattvas, or the world by giving rise to a lowly thought."
Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound said to his Buddha: "World-Honored One, my journey to the Saha world is entirely due to the power of the Tathagata. It is the playful supernatural power of the Tathagata and the adornment of the Tathagata's merits and wisdom."
Then, Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound, without rising from his seat and without his body moving, entered a samadhi. With the power of this samadhi, he transformed eighty-four thousand jeweled lotus flowers not far from the Dharma seat on Mount Vulture Peak. Their stems were of Jambunada gold, their leaves were of white silver, their filaments were of diamond, and their platforms were of kimbulaka jewels.
At that time, the Dharma Prince Mañjuśrī, seeing these lotus flowers, said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, what is the reason for this auspicious sign to appear first? There are thousands of millions of these lotus flowers, with stems of Jambunada gold, leaves of white silver, filaments of diamond, and platforms of kimbulaka jewels."
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha said to Mañjuśrī: "Bodhisattva-Mahāsattva Wonderful Sound, with his retinue of eighty-four thousand Bodhisattvas, wishes to come from the land of the Pure-Flower-Constellation-King-Wisdom Buddha to this Saha world to make offerings to, be close to, and pay homage to me. He also wishes to make offerings to and hear the Lotus Sutra."
Mañjuśrī said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, what roots of goodness did this Bodhisattva plant? What merits did he cultivate to have such great supernatural power? What samadhi does he practice? We wish you would tell us the name of this samadhi. We also wish to diligently cultivate it. By practicing this samadhi, one can see the size and form of this Bodhisattva, and his dignified conduct. We only wish, World-Honored One, that with your supernatural power, you would cause us to see that Bodhisattva when he comes."
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha said to Mañjuśrī: "This long-passed-away Abundant Treasures Tathagata will manifest his form for you all to see him."
Then, Abundant Treasures Buddha said to that Bodhisattva: "Noble man, please come. The Dharma Prince Mañjuśrī wishes to see your body."
At that time, Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound vanished from that land and, along with his eighty-four thousand Bodhisattvas, came forth. As they passed through all the lands, the ground shook in six ways, and they all rained down seven-jeweled lotus flowers. Hundreds of thousands of heavenly music played without being beaten. This Bodhisattva's eyes were like the wide leaves of a blue lotus flower. Even if you were to combine the moon a hundred million times, his face would be even more majestic. His body was of a pure golden color, adorned with immeasurable hundreds of thousands of merits. His majesty was brilliant, and his light was shining. He was complete with all the marks, and his body was as firm as the diamond body of a Narayana. He entered a seven-jeweled tower and rose into the air, seven tāla trees high from the ground. He and his retinue of Bodhisattvas, who were reverently surrounding him, came to Mount Vulture Peak in the Saha world.
When he arrived, he descended from the seven-jeweled tower, held a necklace worth a hundred thousand jewels, and went to Śākyamuni Buddha's place. He bowed his head at the Buddha’s feet, offered the necklace, and said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, the Pure-Flower-Constellation-King-Wisdom Buddha asks about the World-Honored One's well-being: 'Are you in good health and without much sickness? Are you at ease in your daily life? Are your four elements in harmony? Is the world endurable? Are sentient beings easy to convert? Do they not have too much greedy desire, anger, foolishness, jealousy, stinginess, and arrogance? Are they not unfilial to their parents, disrespectful of the śramaṇas, and do they not hold wrong views and have unwholesome minds? Do they not restrain their five senses?'
"World-Honored One, are sentient beings able to subdue all the demon armies? Has the long-passed-away Abundant Treasures Tathagata come to listen to the Dharma in his seven-jeweled stupa? He also asks about Abundant Treasures Tathagata's well-being: 'Is he at peace and without much sickness? Can he endure staying for a long time?' World-Honored One, I now wish to see Abundant Treasures Buddha's body. We only wish that the World-Honored One would show me and cause me to see it."
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha said to Abundant Treasures Buddha: "This Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound wishes to see you."
Then, Abundant Treasures Buddha said to Wonderful Sound: "Excellent! Excellent! You were able to come here to make offerings to Śākyamuni Buddha, and to hear the Lotus Sutra, and also to see Mañjuśrī and the others."
At that time, Bodhisattva Flower-Virtue said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, what roots of goodness did this Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound plant? What merits did he cultivate to have such supernatural power?"
The Buddha said to Bodhisattva Flower-Virtue: "In the past, there was a Buddha named King of Cloud-Thunder-Voice Tathagata, Worthy One, Truly and Universally Enlightened, Perfect in Knowledge and Conduct, Well-Gone, Knower of the World, Supreme Being, Tamer of Men, Teacher of Gods and Humans, Buddha, World-Honored One. His land was named Manifesting-All-Worlds, and the kalpa was named Rejoice-in-Seeing.
"Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound, for twelve thousand years, used a hundred thousand kinds of music to make offerings to the King of Cloud-Thunder-Voice Buddha and also offered him eighty-four thousand seven-jeweled bowls. Because of this karmic reward, he is now born in the land of the Pure-Flower-Constellation-King-Wisdom Buddha and has this supernatural power. Flower-Virtue, what do you think? Was the Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound who made offerings of music and offered the jeweled bowls to the King of Cloud-Thunder-Voice Buddha a different person? He is this very Bodhisattva-Mahāsattva Wonderful Sound. Flower-Virtue, this Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound has made offerings to and been close to immeasurable Buddhas and has long planted roots of virtue. He has also encountered hundreds of thousands of millions of nayuta Buddhas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges."
"Flower-Virtue, you only see Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound's body here, but this Bodhisattva manifests various bodies everywhere to preach this scripture for all sentient beings. He may appear as a Brahma King, as Śakra, as a Sovereign of the Devas, as a Great Sovereign of the Devas, as a great heavenly general, as the heavenly king Vaiśravaṇa, as a wheel-turning holy king, as a small king, as an elder, as a householder, as a government official, as a Brahmin, as a monk, a nun, a layman, or a laywoman. He may appear as the wife of an elder, a householder, or a government official, or as the wife of a Brahmin. He may appear as a boy or a girl. He may appear as a god, a dragon, a yaksha, a gandharva, an asura, a garuda, a kinnara, a mahoraga, a human, or a non-human to preach this sutra. He is able to save those in the hells, the hungry ghost realm, the animal realm, and all difficult places. He can even transform into a woman to preach this sutra in the king's palace."
"Flower-Virtue, this Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound is able to save and protect all sentient beings in the Saha world. The various forms this Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound manifests in this Saha land to preach this scripture for sentient beings do not diminish his supernatural powers, transformations, or wisdom. With various kinds of wisdom, this Bodhisattva illuminates the Saha world and causes all sentient beings to know what they should know. In worlds as numerous as the sands of the Ganges in the ten directions, he also does the same. If a person should be saved by the form of a śrāvaka, he appears as a śrāvaka to preach the Dharma for them. If they should be saved by the form of a pratyekabuddha, he appears as a pratyekabuddha. If they should be saved by the form of a Bodhisattva, he appears as a Bodhisattva. If they should be saved by the form of a Buddha, he appears as a Buddha. In this way, according to who should be saved, he manifests his form for them. Even if they should be saved by entering extinction, he manifests extinction for them. Flower-Virtue, the story of Bodhisattva-Mahāsattva Wonderful Sound's attainment of great supernatural powers and the power of wisdom is like this."
At that time, Bodhisattva Flower-Virtue said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, this Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound has planted deep roots of goodness. World-Honored One, in what samadhi does this Bodhisattva dwell that he can manifest such transformations to save and liberate sentient beings?"
The Buddha said to Bodhisattva Flower-Virtue: "Noble man, that samadhi is named the Samadhi of Manifesting All Forms. Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound dwells in this samadhi and is able to bring such benefits to countless sentient beings."
When this chapter on Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound was being preached, eighty-four thousand people who had come with him all attained the Samadhi of Manifesting All Forms. And the countless Bodhisattvas of this Saha world also attained this samadhi and dhāranīs.
At that time, Bodhisattva-Mahāsattva Wonderful Sound, having made offerings to Śākyamuni Buddha and the stupa of Abundant Treasures Buddha, returned to his home land. As he passed through the various lands, the ground shook in six ways, and jeweled lotus flowers rained down. A hundred million millions of various kinds of music played. When he arrived in his home land, he and his eighty-four thousand Bodhisattvas, surrounded by their retinue, went to the Pure-Flower-Constellation-King-Wisdom Buddha's place. He said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I went to the Saha world and benefited sentient beings. I saw Śākyamuni Buddha and the stupa of Abundant Treasures Buddha, and I paid homage and made offerings. I also saw the Dharma Prince Bodhisattva Mañjuśrī, and I saw Bodhisattva Medicine King, Bodhisattva Diligence, and Bodhisattva Valiant-Giver. I also enabled these eighty-four thousand Bodhisattvas to attain the Samadhi of Manifesting All Forms."
When this chapter on the travels of Bodhisattva Wonderful Sound was being preached, forty-two thousand heavenly beings attained the patience of non-arising, and Bodhisattva Flower-Virtue attained the Samadhi of the Lotus Sutra.

Chapter 25: The Universal Gateway of the Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara
At that time, Bodhisattva Boundless Intent rose from his seat, bared his right shoulder, and, with palms joined, said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, for what reason is Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara called Avalokiteśvara?"
The Buddha said to Bodhisattva Boundless Intent: "Noble man, if there are immeasurable hundreds of thousands of millions of sentient beings who suffer from all kinds of afflictions, and they hear of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara and with a single mind call his name, Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara will immediately perceive their voices and they will all be liberated.
"If a person upholds the name of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, and even enters a great fire, the fire will not be able to burn them, because of the majestic and spiritual power of this Bodhisattva. If they are swept away by a great flood, and they call his name, they will immediately reach a shallow place. If there are hundreds of thousands of millions of sentient beings who, for the sake of seeking treasures like gold, silver, lapis lazuli, tridacna, agate, coral, amber, and pearls, enter the great ocean, and if a black wind blows their ships and causes them to drift into the land of the Rakshasa demons, and if even one person among them calls the name of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, all these people will be liberated from the dangers of the Rakshasas. It is for this reason that he is called Avalokiteśvara (the one who perceives the sound)."
"If there is a person who is about to be harmed, and they call the name of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, the knives and sticks in the hands of the person trying to harm them will immediately break into pieces, and they will be liberated. If the three-thousand-great-thousand-fold world is filled with yakshas and rakshasas who want to torment a person, and they hear that person call the name of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, these evil ghosts will not even be able to look at them with evil eyes, let alone harm them.
"If there is a person, whether they are guilty or not, whose body is bound by shackles, chains, and manacles, and they call the name of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, all of these will be broken and they will immediately be liberated. If the three-thousand-great-thousand-fold world is filled with hostile bandits, and there is a caravan leader who is guiding many merchants with valuable treasures through a dangerous road, and one person among them proclaims: 'All you noble men, do not be afraid! You should all, with a single mind, call the name of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara! This Bodhisattva is able to grant fearlessness to sentient beings. If you call his name, you will be liberated from these hostile bandits.' When the merchants hear this, they will all call out: 'Namo Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara!' Because they call his name, they will immediately be liberated."
"Boundless Intent, the majestic and spiritual power of Bodhisattva-Mahāsattva Avalokiteśvara is so great. If there is a sentient being who is filled with greedy desire and they constantly remember and revere Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, they will be freed from desire. If they are filled with anger and constantly remember and revere Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, they will be freed from anger. If they are filled with foolishness and constantly remember and revere Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, they will be freed from foolishness.
"Boundless Intent, Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara has such great majestic and spiritual power and brings great benefit to many. For this reason, all sentient beings should constantly think of him. If a woman wishes to have a son, and she bows and makes offerings to Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, she will give birth to a son who is blessed with virtues and wisdom. If she wishes to have a daughter, she will give birth to a daughter who is beautiful and has good marks, who has planted roots of virtue in past lives, and who is loved and revered by all. Boundless Intent, Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara has such power. If a sentient being reverently bows and makes offerings to Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, their blessings will not be in vain. For this reason, all sentient beings should receive and uphold the name of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara."
"Boundless Intent, if a person were to receive and uphold the names of sixty-two million Bodhisattvas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges, and for their entire life, they were to make offerings of food, clothing, bedding, and medicine, what do you think? Is the merit of this noble man or noble woman great?"
Boundless Intent said: "Very great, World-Honored One."
The Buddha said: "If a person receives and upholds the name of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara and even for a short time, bows and makes offerings, the blessings of these two people are exactly equal and cannot be exhausted even in hundreds of thousands of millions of kalpas. Boundless Intent, by receiving and upholding the name of Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, one attains such immeasurable and boundless blessings and benefits."
The Manifestations of Avalokiteśvara
Bodhisattva Boundless Intent said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, how does Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara travel in this Saha world? How does he preach the Dharma for sentient beings? What is the matter of his power of expedient means?"
The Buddha said to Bodhisattva Boundless Intent: "Noble man, in a certain land, if sentient beings should be saved by the form of a Buddha, Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara will immediately manifest as a Buddha to preach the Dharma for them. If they should be saved by the form of a pratyekabuddha, he will immediately manifest as a pratyekabuddha to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a śrāvaka, he will immediately manifest as a śrāvaka to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a Brahma King, he will immediately manifest as a Brahma King to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a Śakra, he will immediately manifest as a Śakra to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a Sovereign of the Devas, he will immediately manifest as a Sovereign of the Devas to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a Great Sovereign of the Devas, he will immediately manifest as a Great Sovereign of the Devas to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a great heavenly general, he will immediately manifest as a great heavenly general to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of Vaiśravaṇa, he will immediately manifest as Vaiśravaṇa to preach the Dharma.
"If they should be saved by the form of a small king, he will immediately manifest as a small king to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of an elder, he will immediately manifest as an elder to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a householder, he will immediately manifest as a householder to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a government official, he will immediately manifest as a government official to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a Brahmin, he will immediately manifest as a Brahmin to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a monk, nun, layman, or laywoman, he will immediately manifest as a monk, nun, layman, or laywoman to preach the Dharma.
"If they should be saved by the form of the wife of an elder, a householder, a government official, or a Brahmin, he will immediately manifest as a woman to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a boy or a girl, he will immediately manifest as a boy or a girl to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a god, a dragon, a yaksha, a gandharva, an asura, a garuda, a kinnara, a mahoraga, a human, or a non-human, he will immediately manifest as such to preach the Dharma. If they should be saved by the form of a vajra-holding deity, he will immediately manifest as a vajra-holding deity to preach the Dharma."
"Boundless Intent, Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara is complete in these merits and, with various forms, travels to all lands to save and liberate sentient beings. For this reason, you all should, with a single mind, make offerings to Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara. This Bodhisattva-Mahāsattva Avalokiteśvara is able to grant fearlessness in times of fear and urgent danger. For this reason, in this Saha world, he is also called the Giver of Fearlessness."
Bodhisattva Boundless Intent said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I will now make an offering to Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara." He then took off the jeweled necklace from his neck, worth hundreds of thousands of gold, and gave it to him, saying: "Noble One, please accept this precious jeweled necklace, which is a Dharma offering." At that time, Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara would not accept it.
Boundless Intent again said to Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara: "Noble One, out of compassion for us, please accept this necklace."
At that time, the Buddha said to Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara: "You should have compassion for this Bodhisattva Boundless Intent and the four groups of the assembly, the gods, dragons, yakshas, gandharvas, asuras, garudas, kinnaras, mahoragas, humans, and non-humans, and accept this necklace."
Immediately, Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara, out of compassion for the four groups and the gods, dragons, humans, and non-humans, accepted the necklace. He divided it into two parts. He offered one part to Śākyamuni Buddha and the other part to the stupa of Abundant Treasures Buddha.
"Boundless Intent, Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara has such free and supernatural power and travels in the Saha world."
The Universal Gateway (Verse)
At that time, Bodhisattva Boundless Intent spoke in verse, asking:
The World-Honored One, with them wonderful marks,
I'm askin' you again, about him in the dark:
Tell me, why this Buddha's child, so true and grand,
Is called Avalokiteśvara, throughout the land?

The Honored One, with them wonderful marks so fine,
Answered Boundless Intent, with a verse and a sign:
"Listen to the practices of Avalokiteśvara, hear my plea!
He skillfully responds, for all the world to see.
His great vow is deep, like the ocean's endless blue,
He's been workin' at it for kalpas, it's true.
Served a hundred thousand million Buddhas, so they say,
And gave rise to a pure vow, come what may.

Just a little somethin' I'll tell you 'bout his grace:
If you hear his name, or see his gentle face,
And you think of him in your heart, it ain't in vain,
He can wash away the suffering, ease all the pain.
If a bad heart rises, full of spite and dread,
And pushes you down, into a fiery bed,
Just think of Avalokiteśvara, his power strong and deep,
That fire pit turns to a pond, while you softly sleep.

Or if you're swept away, in the ocean's mighty hold,
With dragons, fish, and ghosts, a story to be told,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power takes its flight,
The waves won't drag you down, in the darkest night.
Or on Mount Sumeru's top, so high and grand,
And someone shoves you over, with a cruel, harsh hand,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power you will find,
You'll stand still like the sun, leaving troubles behind.

If an evil person chases, with a hateful eye,
And you fall from Diamond Mountain, beneath the sky,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power will take hold,
Not a single hair will be harmed, or so I've been told.
Or if hostile bandits surround you, a fearsome crew,
With knives held sharp to harm you, what will you do?
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power will set things right,
They'll feel compassion risin', in the fading light.

If a king brings danger, and the axe is near,
And execution's waitin', filled with doubt and fear,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power will be seen,
That knife will break to pieces, sharp and keen.
Or if you're chained and manacled, your hands and feet are bound,
No freedom in your movement, on the cold, hard ground,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power will shine through,
You'll be freed and liberated, what else can you do?

If curses come to harm you, dark and full of dread,
And all kinds of poisons, buzzing 'round your head,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power will make a turn,
The harm goes back to sender, a lesson they will learn.
Or if you meet them rakshasas, with a fearsome grin,
Poisonous dragons, or ghosts, where do you begin?
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power strong and true,
They won't dare to harm you, me and you.

If evil beasts surround you, with sharp teeth and claws,
A frightening sight to see, against all natural laws,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power will take flight,
They'll run to the distance, in the fading light.
Vipers, snakes, and scorpions, with breath like burning smoke,
A poisonous vapor rising, a choking, silent joke,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power will be heard,
They'll go away when they hear you, without another word.

When clouds roll in, with thunder and the lightning's flash,
And hail and heavy rain falls, in a mighty, sudden crash,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power will come fast,
It'll be dispelled immediately, a memory of the past.
Sentient beings in trouble, with suffering all around,
His wonderful, wise power, on holy ground,
Can save 'em from the worldly pains, so deep and vast,
His mercy and his wisdom, forever they will last.

He's got the power of spirits, beyond compare,
Cultivates wisdom widely, and means beyond all care.
In all the lands of ten directions, far and wide they roam,
There's no place he don't manifest, always bringin' it home.
In all the evil destinies, the Hells and ghosts and beasts,
The pain of birth and aging, sickness, and death's feasts,
He gradually extinguishes 'em all, with a gentle hand,
Bringin' peace and solace, across the land.

The true perception, pure and bright, a guiding star,
The great perception of wisdom, shining from afar.
The perception of compassion, and of love so sweet,
We ought to always wish for these, at his sacred feet.
The pure and unconditioned light, a sun so grand and bold,
Breaks all the darkness, a story to be told.
Can conquer winds of disaster, and the fiery flame,
Illuminating the world, whisperin' his name.

His body of compassion, like a thunderous drum's deep sound,
His wonderful, compassionate mind, like clouds upon the ground,
He pours down Dharma rain, like sweet and gentle dew,
Extinguishes afflictions' flames, for me and for you.
When arguments and lawsuits, in the courthouse ring,
Or in a fearful army, a fearful song they sing,
If you think of Avalokiteśvara, his power will descend,
All the enemies scatter, right up to the end.

His is the wonderful voice, Avalokiteśvara's call,
The voice of Brahma, the sea-tide, standing tall.
Superior to all worldly voices, strong and clear and true,
For this reason, you must always think of him, me and you.
In every single thought, don't let no doubt arise,
The pure and holy Avalokiteśvara, before your very eyes,
Can be our refuge, in times of sorrow and of pain,
When death's danger lingers, he'll bring the sun again.

He's got all the merits, a boundless, endless sea,
He sees all sentient beings, with compassion, wild and free.
His sea of blessings, immeasurable and grand,
For this reason, we should pay him homage, throughout the land.
At that time, Bodhisattva Earth-Holder rose from his seat and said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, if a sentient being hears this chapter on Bodhisattva Avalokiteśvara's free and independent work, and his power to manifest in a universal gateway, you should know that the merit of this person is not small."
When the Buddha preached this chapter of the universal gateway, eighty-four thousand sentient beings in the assembly all gave rise to the unequaled mind of Anuttara-samyak-sambodhi.
Chapter 26: Dharanis

At that time, Bodhisattva Medicine King rose from his seat, bared his right shoulder, and, with palms joined, said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, if a noble man or noble woman is able to uphold the Lotus Sutra—whether they read, recite, and master it, or copy the sutra scrolls—how much merit do they attain?"
The Buddha said to Medicine King: "If a noble man or noble woman makes offerings to Buddhas as numerous as the sands of sixty-two hundred million Ganges Rivers, what do you think? Is the merit they attain great?"
"Very great, World-Honored One."
The Buddha said: "If a noble man or noble woman is able to uphold even a four-line verse of this sutra, and reads, recites, understands its meaning, and practices it as it is taught, their merit is very great."
At that time, Bodhisattva Medicine King said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I will now give the Dharma teacher a dhāraṇī spell to protect him." He then spoke the spell:
An-er, Man-er, Mo-ni, Mo-mo-ni, Zhi-li, Zha-li-di, She-wei, She-li-duo-wei, Shan-di, Mu-di, Mu-duo-li, Suo-li, A-wei-suo-fu, Sang-li, Suo-li, Cha-yi, A-cha-yi, A-qi-ni, Shan-di, She-li, Tuo-luo-ni, A-lu-qie-po-suo-po-zha-bi-sha-ni, Ni-pi-ti, A-bian-duo-luo-ni-li-ti, A-dan-duo-bo-li-shu-di, Ou-jiu-li, Mu-jiu-li, A-luo-li, Bo-luo-li, Shou-jia-cha, A-san-mo-san-li, Fo-tuo-bi-ji-li-ti, Da-mo-bo-li-cha-ti, Seng-qie-ni-qu-sha-ni, Po-she-po-she-shu-di, Man-duo-luo, Man-duo-luo-cha-ye-duo, You-lou-duo, You-lou-duo-qiao-she-lüe, E-cha-luo, E-cha-ye-duo-ye, A-po-luo, A-mo-ruo-na-duo-ye.
"World-Honored One, this dhāraṇī spell was spoken by Buddhas as numerous as the sands of sixty-two hundred million Ganges Rivers. If anyone harms or slanders this Dharma teacher, they are harming and slandering all these Buddhas."
At that time, Śākyamuni Buddha praised Bodhisattva Medicine King, saying: "Excellent! Excellent, Medicine King! Because you have compassionately protected this Dharma teacher, you have spoken this dhāraṇī, which brings great benefit to sentient beings."
At that time, Bodhisattva Valiant Giver said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I also, for the sake of protecting those who read, recite, and uphold the Lotus Sutra, will speak a dhāraṇī. If this Dharma teacher attains this dhāraṇī, no yakshas, rakshasas, pūtanas, kṛtyas, kumbhāṇḍas, or hungry ghosts will be able to find a weakness to attack him." He then spoke the spell in the presence of the Buddha:
Zuo-li, Mo-he-zuo-li, Yu-zhi, Mu-zhi, A-li, A-luo-po-di, Nie-li-di, Nie-li-duo-po-di, Yi-zhi-ni, Wei-zhi-ni, Zhi-chi-ni, Nie-li-chi-ni, Nie-li-chi-po-di.
"World-Honored One, this dhāraṇī spell was spoken by Buddhas as numerous as the sands of the Ganges. They all rejoiced in it. If anyone harms or slanders this Dharma teacher, they are harming and slandering all these Buddhas."
At that time, the world-protecting Heavenly King Vaiśravaṇa said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I also, out of compassion for sentient beings and to protect this Dharma teacher, will speak a dhāraṇī." He then spoke the spell:
A-li, Na-li, Tuo-na-li, A-na-lu, Na-li, Ju-na-fu.
"World-Honored One, with this divine spell, I will protect the Dharma teacher. I myself will also protect the one who upholds this sutra, so that within a hundred yojanas, they will have no misfortune."
At that time, the Heavenly King Dhṛtarāṣṭra was in the assembly with his retinue of tens of millions of nayuta gandharva beings. With reverence, they all went before the Buddha, joined their palms, and said to the Buddha: "World-Honored One, I also, with a divine dhāraṇī spell, will protect the one who upholds the Lotus Sutra." He then spoke the spell:
A-jia-ni, Jia-ni, Qu-li, Gan-tuo-li, Zhan-tuo-li, Mo-deng-qi, Chang-qiu-li, Fu-lou-suo-ni, E-di.
"World-Honored One, this dhāraṇī spell was spoken by forty-two hundred million Buddhas. If anyone harms or slanders this Dharma teacher, they are harming and slandering all these Buddhas."
The Vow of the Rakshasa Maidens
At that time, there were ten rakshasa maidens, whose names were Lamva, Vilamva, Crooked-Tooth, Flower-Tooth, Black-Tooth, Many-Hairs, Endless-Stomach, Upholder-of-Garlands, Kunti, and Seizer-of-the-Essence-of-All-Beings. These ten rakshasa maidens, along with the Mother of Demon Children, and their sons and retinues, all went to the Buddha's place. With one voice, they said to the Buddha:
"World-Honored One, we also wish to protect those who read, recite, and uphold the Lotus Sutra and to remove their misfortunes. If there are those who seek to find a weakness in the Dharma teacher, we will prevent them from having an advantage." They then spoke the spell in the presence of the Buddha:
Yi-ti-li, Yi-ti-min, Yi-ti-li, A-di-li, Yi-ti-li, Ni-li, Ni-li, Ni-li, Ni-li, Ni-li, Lou-xi, Lou-xi, Lou-xi, Lou-xi, Duo-xi, Duo-xi, Duo-xi, Dou-xi, Nu-xi.
"It is better that someone climb on our heads than to trouble a Dharma teacher. No yakshas, rakshasas, hungry ghosts, pūtanas, kṛtyas, vetālas, gandhas, unmādas, apasmāras, yaksha-kṛtyas, human-kṛtyas, or those with fevers of one day, two days, three days, four days, or up to seven days, or those with constant fevers; whether they have the form of a man, a woman, a boy, or a girl—even in a dream, they shall not trouble him."
They then spoke in verse in the presence of the Buddha:
If you don't heed this righteous plea,
And trouble the one who preaches free,
Your head will split, believe it true,
Like an āralu branch, through and through.

The sin you'll bear, a heavy toll,
Like killing kin, it'll haunt your soul.
Like pressing oil, a grinding plight,
